*  무단  배포  및  상업적  이용  금지

무단  배포  시  불합격..  이라  말하고  싶을  정도로  여러분의  눈이  빠지도록  정성을  담은  노력과  시간이

깃든  자료입니다.  우리가  ‘다  함께’  만든  자료임을  잊지  말아주세요.  그럼에도  지키지  않으신다면,  훗

날  선생님의  복기본을  무단  재배포하고,  돈  주고  파는  선생님이  꼭  계시리라,  더불어  선생님의  교무실

에  역대급  빌런이  함께하리라  믿겠습니다.  수고해주셔서  정말  감사드립니다.  올해  꼭  합격합시다!

various jobs in magazines and sharing their dream jobs. In Lesson 5, students will be able to enhance
higher-level cognitive skills with thinking about the story’s structure and predicting possible endings.
S2 performed word master using online dictionary. S2 shared the meaning of new word. ‘crane’, with
picture with other students. Teacher sued the tool, graphic organizer. He helped students compare
and contrast between two families by completing the figure.

10  S1 is in the stage 5. S1 extends the use of ‘can’ with other various verbs, share, speak including have,

In Step 2, teacher just tells and explains and students listen to the teacher’s stories in anecdotal formats
rather than developing integrated language skills. In Step 4, teacher explains the meanings of new
words with synonyms and antonyms without cultural connotations of new words.
action research
The  problems  are  uneven  participation  and  mother-tongue  use.  Jigsaw  can  increase  the  students’
overall participation since they have to pool all their information to complete their group task without
free-riders. Having a monitor student in a group makes students put more effort to use English while
teacher is not present.
Content and organization were two categories. Jinhee added more details of the story to support the
fact that her family ate delicious snacks such as her brother got three cups of ice cream and she got
strawberry cake. She used liking words for a logical sequence of events such as ‘but’, ‘then’, and ‘so’.
Teaching procedure 1 focuses on Collocation. Students choose the words which co-occur with the
verbs  ‘do’  and  ‘make’  and  find  more  examples  in  the  online  concordancer.  Teaching  procedure  2
focuses  on  Grammar.  Students  identify  countable  and  uncountable  words  and  choose  appropriate
quantifiable expressions for each noun.
For  guideline  2,  Item  1  is  revised.  The  teacher  revises  the  stem  as  simple  and  direct  to  make  the
question  clear.  For Guideline  3,  Item  3  is  revised.  The  problem  is clearly  suggested  about  what  to

Computer adaptive testing
In lesson 2, the objective is to encourage learners to tap into their own lives in that Ms. Lee wants to
increase the relevance of the contents or activities in relation to the students’ experiences by using
magazine  pictures  of  various  jobs  along  with  some  pictures  related  to  jobs  in  the  textbook  and  by
asking them to share their dream jobs. In lesson 5, the objective is to enhance higher-level cognitive
skills  since  Ms.  Lee  wants  to  adapt  materials  in  such  a  way as  to  require  students  to  hypothesize,
predict,  or  infer  by  editing  the  story,  intentionally  deleting  a  few  sentences  at  the  end  and  by
challenging the students to think about the story’s structure and look ahead to possible endings using
the storyline.
The S2’s role is ‘word master’ in that S2 shows the meaning of the word, ‘crane’ when one student
asks. The tool is ‘graphic organizer’ since Ms. Han used it to help students to comprehend the story
about the Garcia and the Brown families while reading.

The steps 2 and 4 do not correspond to the suggestions. In the step 2, the teacher needs to teach
culture while involving the integration of the four language skills and should not limit cultural instruction
to lecture or anecdotal formats, but the teacher tells students about the origins of the world-famous
holidays,  explains  the  cultural  characteristics  of  them,  and  shares  his  experiences  related  to  the
holidays while students are just listening to the teacher’s stories. And in the step 4, the teacher should
use cultural information when teaching vocabulary and teach students about the cultural connotations
of new words, but the teacher explains the meaning of the words, comparing them with their synonyms
and/or  antonyms  while  the  students  are  noting  the  words  and  memorizing  them  using  mnemonic
devices.
action research
The two problems are uneven participation and mother-tongue use. As for uneven participation, jigsaw
task can increase students’ participation when they pool the information in groups, preventing students
from free-riding without contribution to the discussion. As for mother-tongue use, appointing a monitor
raises awareness of somebody’s monitoring which helps them make more efforts in using the target
language, preventing them from using the same mother tongue in group work, even when Ms. Hong
is far away.
One category is ‘content’ in that Jinhee revised her draft by adding more details about eating delicious
snacks as in ‘Both my brother and I love sweets.’ The other category is ‘organization’ since Jinhee

Teaching procedure 1 focuses on ‘collocation’ in that it asks students to choose which expressions are
possible with the words ‘do’ and ‘make’. Teaching procedure 2 focuses on ‘grammar’ since it asks
students to identify countable and uncountable nouns and to choose the expression of quantity that
does not fit with the word ‘results’.
The item 1 is revised according to the guideline 2 in that the teacher revised the stem as simply and
directly as possible by removing the two sentences in the original stem. The item 3 is revised according
to the guideline 3 since the teacher revised the stem to present a single clearly formulated problem of
indirect question to avoid mixed content of tense and indirect question by removing ‘where’ in the
original stem and changing ‘have’ into ‘had’ in the original options.
-sonorant
The words in (b) and (d) can be nonsense words. Words with simple onset are more English-like than
those with complex onset, and words with complex onset that show progressively increasing sonority
values are more English-like than those that show progressively decreasing sonority values.
The sentence (3b) has a structurally unavailable reading, and the sentence (4a) is ungrammatical. In
(4), the sentence adverb ‘surely’ is within the VP, and in order for it to adjoin to the S node, it has to
cross a branch.
preposition, adverb
Penultimate, trochaic
The noun-forming suffix ‘-al’ can attach to verb stems that have the primary stress on the ultimate
syllable.
The  phrasal  coordination  in  the  sentence  (4b)  shows  different  truth  conditions  from  the  clausal
coordination like ‘The last objection concerned the cost, and the most telling objection concerned the
cost.' If the sentence of the clausal coordination is true, we cannot say that (4b) is true.
-sonorant
The two nonsense words are rviss and nkob. The sonority in the complex onset must rise towards the
nucleus in English.
They are (3b) and (4a), respectively. In (4a), because not is a SpecVP, the following surely is within the
VP, but adjoins to the S node. Thus, surely crosses the VP branch, violating the NCB constraint.

It is (4b). Its appropriate clausal coordination is ‘The last objection concerned the cost and the most
telling objection concerned the cost’. (4b) is true when there is a single objection concerning the cost.
However, its clause coordination is true when there are two separate objections concerning the cost.
Thus, they have different truth conditions.

There are two causes of tunnel vision that learners or readers experience. The first cause is an overall
lack of contextual and/or background knowledge. The second cause is bad reading habits, especially
slow reading. In conclusion, the learner should increase knowledge and the reader should speed up
to cure tunnel vision.

-to put my interest before that of others

-Tunnel vision in the cognitive realm occurs when our attention is narrowed to one or two trivial details
oblivious to bigger context. There are two major causes of tunnel vision. First, an overall deprivation
of background information is the prime culprit of this cognitive flaw. The second cause of cognitive
tunnel vision is poor reading skills; slow reading is the commonest of all. In conclusion, compensating
for a lack in background knowledge and speeding up our reading might be a solution to our tunnel
vision.
-When our attention is narrowed to one or two trivial details ignoring bigger context, we suffer tunnel
vision in the cognitive domain. Our narrowed cognitive sight hampers our intellectual receptivity. The
two prime causes of tunnel vision are as follows: an overall deprivation of background information and
poor reading skills. When we lack background knowledge, we fail to see the woods, hindering our
acquisition of knowledge while slow reading prevents our brain from concentrating on the task at hand.
In conclusion, increasing background knowledge and speeding up our reading may enable us to deal
with our tunnel vision more effectively.
knowledge

participants in the scene.
-The underlined part means that we choose to remain passive observers not actively participating in
the act.

First,  in  <B>  the  two  nonsense  words  are  (b)  rviss  and  (d)  nkob.  Second,  the  one  phonological
generalization is that in English the words with simple onset and complex onset (or onset clusters)
have sonority increasing gradually towards the peak of the syllable (or the nucleus).
First,  in  <B>  the  structurally  unavailable  reading  is  (3b)  and  the  ungrammatical  sentence  is  (4a).
Second, in (4a), in tree diagrams the sentence adverb ‘surely’ which adjoins to the S node cannot
occur between the word ‘not’ which merges at SpecVP and the V-bar ‘break his promise’; the adverb
‘surely’ ends up crossing the VP branch to adjoin to the S node, violating the NCB constraint.

Lesson  2  encourages  learners  to  tap  into  their  own  lives  while  Lesson  5  enhances  higher-level

The phonological generalization is that the noun-forming suffix ‘-al’ can attach to the verb stem that

First, the phrasal coordination in (4b) shows different truth conditions from the clausal coordination.
The appropriate clausal coordination is as follows: [The last objection concerned the cost] and [the
most telling objection concerned the cost]. Second, under the condition where there are two different
objections, the clausal coordination is true, but the phrasal coordination in (4b) is false. Sentence (4b)
is true when there is only one objection. Therefore, they do not share the same truth conditions.
Ms. Hong asks for Mr. Park's advice about two problems, uneven participation’ and
"mother-tongue  use.’  Thus,  he  is  convinced  that  a  jigsaw  significantly  increases  overall  students’
participation. Also, he thinks that the very awareness that someone is monitoring pushes students to
use the target language, instead of their mother tongue.
Jinhee revises the second draft in terms of content and organization. First, she provides supporting

Tunnel vision has two major causes. First, in cases where background information is lacking, a learner
can lose track of the larger flow of a subject. Second, slow reading can cause tunnel vision when a
learner focuses too much on a part of the text. In conclusion, building up contextual knowledge and
speeding up reading can cure one's tunnel vision.

Two nonsense words are b. rviss and d. nkob. The one generalization of (1) is that words with
simple onset like bod, timp, and rog are more English-like than those with complex onset like mbotto,
and in case of words with complex onset, the second consonant like /l/ of shliz and zloog must be
higher in sonority (more resonant) than the first consonant like /ʃ, z/ of shliz and zloog.
The ONE structurally unavailable reading is (3b). The ONE ungrammatical sentence is (4a). The adverb
surely in (4a), which must attach to the S node, attaches to a node under the VP, so it
violates NCB constraint.
The objective of Ms. Lee’s material adaption for Lesson 2 is to encourage learners to tap into their own
lives. To increase the relevance of the contents of her materials, she uses magazine.
pictures of various jobs as a springboard to get the students in groups to think about the varied jobs
in the world and share their own dream jobs. The objective for Lesson 5 is to enhance higher-level
cognitive skills. She intentionally deletes a few sentences at the end to ask her students to predict
possible endings based on the storyline.
S2 took the role of Word Master, and Mr. Han used a graphic organizer. To play the role of Word Master,
S2 showed the meaning of a new word, ‘crane’, to his classmate by sharing its
picture and meaning from an online dictionary. To use a graphic organizer, Mr. Han asked the students
to complete a venn diagram of Family History that compares and contrasts the Garcia and the Brown
families to get them extract the relevant information from the text.

4  ①  penultimate  ②  trochaic

The noun-forming suffix -al can attach to a verb stem that has the primary stress on the ultimate syllable
― that has the iambic foot structure.
(4b) is the one phrasal coordination that shows different truth conditions from the clausal coordination.
The clausal coordination is “[The last concerned the cost] and [The most telling objection concerned
the cost].” Under the condition where there was a single objection which was the last and most telling
objection,  the  phrasal  coordination  is  true(;  the  clausal  coordination  is  false),  while  the  clausal
coordination is true (; and the phrasal coordination is false) under the condition where there were two
(different) objections, one of which indicates the last objection but the other of which indicates the
most telling objection.
The Ms. Hong’s two problems uneven participation and mother-tongue use. The teacher can solve
uneven participation of the students because jigsaw requires the students to pool the information each
member of a group is responsible for to be able to complete the task. Also, teacher can solve the
problem of mother-tongue use when one of the members in each group is appointed as a monitor
whose role is to make sure that their group members are using the target language.
The two categories are content and organization. With content, Jinhee adds some more details about
the delicious snacks that he his brother had. He specifies the fact that his brother got three cups of ice
cream and he got strawberry cake. With organization, Jinhee improves a logical sequence of events
with the use of linking words such as “Then”, “but”, and “so”.
There are two possible reasons that make people experience tunnel vision. First, one could experience
tunnel vision when they do not possess general background or contextual knowledge. Second, tunnel
vision could also occurs when one reads a text too slowly. The lack of background information and
slow reading habits are the two primary causes of tunnel vision.
knowledge. People rely more on automation that a computer provides than trying to wrestle with a
challenging task for an anticipation of our labors.
Teaching Procedure 1 focuses on collocation because the teacher asks the students to first tick off the
correct  expressions  that  could  come  with  do  and  make,  and  then  asks  them  to  refer  to  an  online
concordancer to find more examples that could co-occur with do and make. Teaching Procedure 2
focuses on Grammar the teacher asks the students to choose the expression of quantify that does not
fit with the noun in each given sentence based on their understanding on countable and uncountable.
Item  1  was  revised  according  to  guideline  2.  The  teacher  makes  the  stem  simple  and  direct  by
removing confounding lexical items such as “sunscreen” and the superfluous sentence, “My forehead
itches every day during the summer. Item 3 was revised according to guideline 3. The teacher presents
a single clearly formulated problem by making where part of options to make the item designed only
to recognize the correct word order of indirect questions.

첨가  전  base의  끝  음절에  강세가  왔었음

(4)  b/  구에서  병렬을  이룰  경우  objection  한  개에  대한  참,  거짓을  따지게  되나,  절에서  병렬을

이루는  문장으로  변형하면  두  개의  objections에  대한  참,  거짓을  따지게  되므로,  두  경우의

진리치는  동일하지  않음

(1) penultimate (2) trochaic. The phonological generalization is that ‘noun-forming suffix –al’ is

(b) in (4) shows different truth conditions from the clausal coordination. The appropriate clausal
coordination is “The last objection concerned the cost and the most telling objection concerned the
cost.” The phrasal and clausal coordination differs in their truth condition because the phrasal
coordination deals with one objection while the clausal coordination deals with two different
objections.
Ms. Hong’s first problem is that there are students who free-ride without contribution during group
activities. To solve this, Mr. Park suggests jigsaw. Jigsaw has students pool all their information in
group, which leads to the increase in overall participation. Her second problem is that students tend
to use the mother tongue in group work while the teacher is not around. To solve this, Mr. Park
suggests appointing a group member as a monitor. Having a monitor in a group helps students use
the target language.
Jinhee revised content and organization in the second draft. For content, she added more detail
about delicious snacks, saying that her brother and she loved sweets and they got ice cream and
strawberry cake. For organization, she used linking words such as ‘but’ and ‘so’. ‘but’ is used to
describe the situation where the writer did but her father did not swim in the pool. Also, ‘so’ is used
to describe the situation where the family were very tired and took a taxi home.

adverb, adjective (-2)  ㅋㅋ  창피하다...
union / The underlined part means to work at Olstead’s to make money. Although he knows the work
at Olstead’s is rough, Oscar wants to work as a temporary worker there. (-2)
penultimate, trochaic / The noun-forming suffix ‘-al’ can attach to the verb that has the primary stress
on the ultimate syllable and has an iambic foot at the end.
(4b). It can be changed into “The last objection concerned the cost and  the most telling objection
concerned the cost.” In the phrasal coordination, both ‘last’ and ‘most’ modify ‘telling’. However, in the
clausal coordination, ‘last’ modifies ‘objection’ but ‘most’ modifies ‘telling’. Thus, (4b) and its clausal
coordination version don’t share the same truth conditions. (–2)
The two problems are ‘uneven participation’ and ‘mother-tongue use’. Mr. Park suggests that Ms. Hong
use a jigsaw task because it increases students’ overall participation significantly as they pool all of
their information in groups. Also, he suggests that Ms. Hong appoint one member of each group as
monitor because when students are aware that they are monitored, they try to use the target language.
content, organization / As for ‘content’, Jinhee adds more details about ‘delicious snacks’. She adds
the third and fourth sentences in the second draft as details. As for ‘organization’, Jinhee uses the
linking word ‘then’ to show a logical sequence of swimming and riding in the second draft. (-1) Linking
word  예시  1개만  씀.  시험장에선  뭐에  홀렸는지  then  하나밖에  안  보였음...
There are two causes of tunnel vision. First, tunnel vision occurs when we lack background and/or
contextual information. Second, poor reading habits such as slow reading cause tunnel vision because
reading  slowly  makes  us  focus  on  individual  letters  and  words.  In  conclusion,  we  should  seek
elsewhere to acquire  the contextual knowledge and increase the reading speed not to experience
tunnel vision.
knowledge / The underlined part means to rely on computer automation for the solutions rather than
wrestle with difficult tasks by ourselves to find our own way to solve them, which makes our desires
meaningful.
Teaching Procedure 1 focuses on ‘collocation’ and Teaching Procedure 2 focuses on ‘grammar’. In
Teaching  Procedure  1,  students  learn  words  that  co-occur  with  ‘do’  and  ‘make’  by  choosing  the
possible  expressions  in  the  given  table  and  referencing  an  online  concordancer.  In  Teaching
Procedure 2, students learn the grammatical feature, countability, of some words, and the proper and
improper expressions of quantity that fits with the noun in each sentence.
Item 3 is revised according to  ➁  and Item 1 is revised according to  ➂. Item 3 states both the stem
and the options simply and directly. The word ‘where’ moves from the stem to options. Item 1 deletes
two sentences and presents a single clearly formulated problem so that there is no mixed content. (-

b. riss [rvɪs], d. nkob [nkob] / In words with complex onset, the first segment of the consonant cluster

First, in (3) in <B>, the sentence (3b) has the structurally unavailable reading. Second, in (4) in <B>,
(4a)  is  ungrammatical.  The  sentence  (4a)  violates  the  NCB  constraint  because  "surely"  cannot  be
located between the SpecVP "not" and the head of the VP "break", which results in branches' crossing
in tree structure. This is because "surely" is a sentence adverb adjoining to the S node [He should not
break his promise], not a VP adverb adjoining to the VP node [not break his promise].
In Lesson 2, Ms. Lee wants to achieve the objective "to encourage learners to tap into their own lives".
Through materials adaptation by using magazine pictures of various jobs along with some pictures
related to jobs in the textbook as a springboard to get students in groups to share their dream jobs,
the teacher increases the relevance of the contents or activities in relation to the students' experiences.
This helps students think about more varied jobs in the real world.
In Lesson 5, Ms. Lee wants to achieve the objective "to enhance higher-level cognitive skills". By editing
the story through intentional deletion of a few sentences at the end, the teacher requires students to
think about the story's structure and predict possible endings, using the storyline.

(4단어  제한) Ms. Hong asked about uneven participation and mother-tongue use. As for the former,
Mr.  Park  made  suggestions  because  students  were  free-riding  without  any  contribution  to  the
discussion.  He  recommended  Ms.  Hong  to  choose  a  jigsaw  task  to  increase  the  students'  overall
participation by pooling all their information in groups.
As for the latter, Mr. Park made suggestions because students tended to use their mother tongue in
group work, especially when the teacher was not nearby. He recommended her to appoint one group
member as monitor to help students use more target language.
content, organization / As for content, Jinhee added more supporting details in the second draft such
as "Both my brother and I love sweets. My brother got three cups of ice cream and I got strawberry
cake." As for organization, she used linking words in "I swimed in the pool, but my father did not swim.",
"Then, we went on the rides.", "We were very tired, so we took a taxi to come home.". She used "but",
"then", and "so" to show a logical sequence of events in the second draft.

(5단어  제한) Tunnel vision, which is the narrowing of the field of vision, has two main causes. First, a
general lack of contextual or background knowledge can cause tunnel vision, resulting in the  losing
track of the larger flow. Second, poor reading habits such as slow reading can cause tunnel vision,
making the brain to stick to too many individual words and letters, which clogs up the visual system.
In conclusion, to cure one's tunnel vision, one must acquire enough background information elsewhere
and speed up one's reading.
knowledge / The underline part means that now we rely on computer automation instead of taking part
in direct action.
Teaching procedure 1 focuses on collocation and teaching procedure 2 focuses on grammar. As for
the former, students choose which expressions in the table are possible, considering the way "do" and
"make" tend to co-occur with other words or expressions. Students also find more examples of this
collocation,  referencing  an  online  concordancer.  As  for  the  latter,  students  identify  countable  and
uncountable nous and choose the expression of quantity that does not fit with the noun "the results"
in each sentence. Then, students can learn that a grammatical structure may be lexically bound, and
lexical items also have grammatical features.
Item 1, Item 3 / In item 1, the stem is stated as simply and directly as possible, such as "I think I'd better
go to the _____ to get my skin checked." by deleting the first two sentences. In item 3, to avoid mixed
content, a single clearly formulated problem was presented by moving "where" from the stem to the
options.

There are two main causes of tunnel vision where people only focus on the small details. The first
cause is lack of background or contextual knowledge in art and physical education, which leads people
to lose track of larger flows of information. The second cause is poor reading habits and slow reading
which clogs up the visual system. Therefore, by extending background knowledge and increasing the
reading speed, tunnel vision can be cured.

The sonority of onset cluster should raise as they become closer to its nucleous. In the word mbotto,
the first onset cluster is a nasal consonant /m/ and the second onset cluster is a stop obstruent /b/. In
the word mvupe, the first onset cluster is a nasal consonant /m/ and the second onset cluster is a
fricative obstruent /v/ hence the sonority decrease as they become closer to their nucleus.
reading (b) in (3) in <B> is unavailable. sentence (b) in (4) is ungrammatical.
In sentence (b) in (4), surely is a sentence adverb and not merges at SpecVP in tree diagram. it cross
branches to modify not hence it violates NCB constraint.

experiences.

Tunnel  vision  has  two  main  causes.  First,  it  is  caused  by  a  lack  of  contextual  and  background
knowledge, especially in physical and art education. Second, it is caused by poor reading habits of
slow reading, which makes the brain obsessively focus on individual features. In conclusion, learning
and acquiring contextual knowledge and increasing the speed of reading are required to overcome
tunnel vision.

There are twin causes of tunnel vision, which narrows the vision due to limited ability of brain. First,

as  slow  reading  obsess  us  with  reading  a  text  in  individual  words.  In  sum,  we  need  to  get  more
contextual knowledge and speed up reading in order to cure tunnel vision.

Doublespeak deliberately makes things look different in several forms. First, inflated language makes
things seem extraordinary such as a “real counterfeit diamond” for a glass stone and a “once in a
lifetime opportunity” for a normal situation. Second, professional language jargon is used by specialists
to novice people in order to express profundity, authority, and prestige as a computer technician’s use
of “power-cycle” without an explanation. To conclude, understanding forms of doublespeak can enable
us to distinguish the reality from what deludes us.

deception
- The reason that the ink-dummy strategy does not work in the air is that the deceptive tactic loses its
power in the air because the lower density of the air makes a pseudomorph of a prey disperse faster
in the air. On the other hand, the reason that the strategy would not likely succeed in the depths of the
sea is that light cannot penetrate into the deep sea, making it impossible for a pseudomorph of a prey
to stand out in the inky-black backdrop of the deep sea.
- The reason that the ink-dummy strategy would not likely succeed in the air is that air is a medium
with a lower density than water and cannot support the pseudomorph of a bird’s prey long enough for
it to escape. On the other hand, the tactic does not work in the deep sea because light cannot penetrate
into the deep sea, making it almost impossible for deep-sea predators to distinguish the pseudomorph
of a prey from the backdrop of inky-black deep sea.
- The ink-dummy strategy would not likely succeed in the air because air is a medium with a lower
density than water and cannot support the pseudomorph of a slug long enough for it to escape and
the strategy does not work in deep sea either because light cannot penetrate into the deep sea, making
it almost impossible for the predators to distinguish the pseudomorph of a prey from the backdrop of
inky-black deep sea.

- The primary purpose of using doublespeak is to make things seem different from what they really
are. One form of doublespeak is using words in an exaggerated way. A case in point is a belt made
out of “genuine imitation leather,” which means that it is not authentic leather. Jargon is also counted
among examples of doublespeak. Jargon is used to enhance efficiency within a specialized community
or to make the members of the group seem more professional than they really are. But it often makes
those  outside  the  group  feel  confused.  Getting  a  clear  picture  of  doublespeak  enables  us  to
differentiate what things really are from what they are designed to mean.
- Doublespeak is a kind of speech skill used to make things appear better than they really are or paint
the picture of things in a different way. And it comes in many different forms. One form of doublespeak
is exaggeration. This type of inflated language is used to make dull things seem extraordinary. For
example,  you  may  describe  a  synthetic  piece  of  jewelry  as  a  “real  counterfeit  diamond.”  Another
version of doublespeak is using jargon. Jargon is originally intended to facilitate the communication
within a certain professional community. However, when jargon is used with those unfamiliar with it, it
gives the users illusory authority. Getting a picture of the nature of doublespeak allows us to distinguish
what things really are and what someone intends to mean by it.

The syllabic consonant [ŋ] is always homorganic with the preceding consonant because there are no
instances of non-homorganicity so far as the syllabic [ŋ] is concerned; it only occurs after velar stops
([k] and [g]) when the syllabic [n] assimilates to the place of articulation of the preceding velar stops.
noun / Sentence (ii) is ungrammatical. It violates Subjacency because the wh-phrasee ‘which actress’
crosses over two bounding nodes, the NP node ‘a picture of’ and the TP node in the main clause.
Crossing  over  more  than  one  bounding  node  in  one  cycle  of  movement  would  result  in
ungrammaticality.

Doublespeak, which is language used to misrepresent things intentionally, has several forms. The first
of doublespeak’s forms comes from inflated language. Inflated language occurs when ordinary things
and situations are given importance they don’t deserve. The second form of doublespeak is jargon. It
comes to pass when professional language is used with those outside of a specialized group to add
prestige to one’s expression. In conclusion, since doublespeak is a common tool used to distort reality,
we, thus, should be aware of various forms of doublespeak.

There  are  several forms  of  doublespeak. First  one  is  inflated  language,  which  is  used  to  make  the
ordinary  thing  seem  extraordinary  and  to  describe  situations,  and  it  gives  a  perception  that  the
situations and things that were not important are important,,(문장그지같이쓴듯). Second one is jargon,
which is used to communicate within a specialized group but gives an air of authority, profundity and
prestige when used with people who don’t know it. In conclusion, knowing the forms and definitions of
doublespeak can contribute to distinguish the reality and whan people wants us to believe.

‘Korean’ in (i) and (ii) should be interpreted as language and nationality, respectively. As to (i), ‘Korean’

Doublespeak, a language carefully designed to make things be considered as something different from
what they actually are, comes in several forms. First, inflated language makes the ordinary materials
and situations seem extraordinary, giving them a perception of importance. Second, jargon gives an
air of authority and profundity when used with people who do not know the professional language. To
sum up, knowing the definition of doublespeak and its forms can help us distinguish what someone
wants to make us believe from the reality.

that they should put more than three sentences together with appropriate connectors.

There are several forms of doublespeak which is used to make something seem different from what it
is. One form is inflated language which is created to make the normal things seem special. The other
form  is  jargon  which  is  used  to  make  communication  within  a  certain  group.  It  occurs  when
professional  languages  are  used  with  laypeople.  In  conclusion,  we  need  to  be  aware  of  the
doublespeak in order to discriminate between something used as a delusion and the reality.

10  Mr. Lee used Test 2 because the test can assess students' abilities to make a simple sentence using
the target form. In the test, students should describe the picture by using the target form. Mr. Min used
Test 4 because the test can assess how well the students put sentences together to write a story by
letting students describe the sequenced pictures with appropriate connectors. (-1 or -2) target form에

Example  1  used  A2  because  it  is  the  reactive  focus  on  form  where  attention  to  form  arises  out  of
students' production and the teacher gave an explicit feedback by using metalanguage. Example 2
used B1 because it is the pre-emptive focus on form where the student made a particular form the
topic of the conversation even though there was no actual problem and the student asked a question

Spanish / The underlined part means the famous poet’s argument that people can only write poems
in  their  mother  tongue.  The  speaker’s  mother  tongue  is  Spanish,  not  English,  so  she  cannot  write
literature  in  English,  and  she  struggles  from  finding  loopholes  or  exceptions  and  turning  back  to
Spanish on each line.
b. disentangle, c. accountability / The rule is that the aspirated stops can appear in the initial position
of the foot.
Korean in (i) should be interpreted as language while Korean in (ii) should be interpreted as nationality.
As  for  (i),  since  ‘Korean’  is  conjoined  by  another  complement  ‘linguistics’,  ‘Korean’  should  be

complement; thus, it means Korean language. As to (ii), ‘the noun  ‘professor’ cannot be replaced by
‘one’ when the modifying noun ‘Korean’ is a complement; thus, ‘Korean’ is an Adjunct, and ‘the Korean
one’ means the professor from Korea.
2nd, 5th / In the 2nd period, students should utilize top-down processing when they listen to a dialogue
and  find  out  the  main  idea.  They  also  use  bottom-up  processing  when  they  conduct  a  sentence
dictation activity that contains the active and passive voice. In the  5th period, students should  use
bottom-up processing when they distinguish sentences that have subject-verb agreement errors. Also,
they should adopt top-down processing when they what will come next while reading the introductory
paragraph.
Mina recommended cognitive strategies to Junho. She asked Junho to use visualization by creating
mental images in his mind to remember what he had learned. Also, she recommended social strategies
to Junho. She asked Junho to have conversations in English with native speakers to clarify the meaning
of unfamiliar expressions.

10  Michael  displays  ‘C1.  offer  an  apology  for  the  conflict’  in  that  after  consideration,  he  comes  to
understand Ken’s position of emphasizing punctuality, admits his fault, expresses his regret, and then
promises to be on time. Maria displays ‘B1. dismiss the conflict that threatened the other’s face’ in that
she decides to go out to the library during the visit of Sue’s friends instead of directly telling Maria her
complaints because she does not want to create an unpleasant situation.
deception / The ink-dummy tactic would not likely succeed in the air because the medium of air is less
dense, and thus it cannot sustain the ink cloud for enough period to permit the escape of animals.
Also, it cannot succeed in the deep sea since the pseudomorph cannot be recognized against the
constant inky-black backdrop, where light penetration is minimal or zero from the surface.

noun / Sentence (ii) is ungrammatical. The wh-phrase ‘which actress’ is moved out of the NP ‘a picture

The words displaying part-whole relations are used in that S1 mentions about the kitchen, the word

repetition of the same content words is exemplified since S1 talks about wallpaper as in “Isn’t it funny
that  wallpaper  is  in  fashion  again?”  and  then  S1  refers  to  wallpaper  in  “And  she  had  the  same
wallpaper.”

9

(classify  같은  단어를  넣었던  것  같은데..)  express  their  taste  about  valuable  artwork  and  bad
artwork, they themselves become subject to the public’s classification. That is, writing criticism means
passing judgment, and exposing their prestige and identity at the risk of under public scrutiny.
Doublespeak, the language carefully designed to make things look different from the reality, can take
several forms. First, inflated language can make the ordinary situations, like traveling experiences, and
things,  like  cheap  imitations,  seem  extraordinary  and  important.  Second,  jargon  can  be  used  by
specialists to novice people in order to express profundity, authority, and prestige. To conclude, we
should be aware of the meaning and forms of doublespeak to distinguish what someone intends us to
believe from the reality.

agreement/ Criticism is related to taste, and it tells what kind of person the critic is because he/she

There  are  two  forms  of  doublespeak.  First,  inflated  language  is  used  to  make  ordinary  things  or
situations seem extraordinary. It gives a sense of importance to things and situations that would not
be considered important normally. Second, jargon is used as a doublespeak when used with people
that are not “in-the-know”. It is used to give a sense of profundity, prestige, and authority. In conclusion,
being  aware  of  the  meaning  and  forms  of  doublespeak,  which  is  prevalent  in  our  lives,  helps  us

4.-sonorant , -syllabic (-1)/ syllabic [ŋ] is always homorganic with the preceding consonant because it

noun/ (2) is ungrammatical because when ‘which actress’ undergoes the second cycle, it crosses over

Activity 1 focuses on construction in that it requires students to focus on    how posters are typically
constructed  by  asking  why  some  words  of  posters  are  capitalized  and  whether  they  used  full
sentences.  Activity  2  focuses  on  context  in  that  it  requires  students  to  focus  on  the  situation  and
audience by asking questions like “who do you think the review is aimed at?” and “when would people
write this kind of text?”
convergence(-2)/ The underlined part means that critics struggle to terms with what they do not exactly
know  how  to  deal  with,  passing  judgment,  exposing  themselves,  and  putting  their  identities  and
prestiges at risk.
Doublespeak, which is a language designed to make things different from reality, comes in several
forms. First, inflated language that makes ordinary things seem extraordinary is one of doublespeaks.
It  can  be  used  when  describing  cheap  material  or  situations.  Second,  jargon  can  be  used  as
doublespeak when people use professional language with people who are not professional, giving an
air of profundity, prestige and authority. For example, if a computer technician says the professional
term “power-cycle” instead of easier terms, he is using jargon as doublespeak. To conclude, keeping
awareness of the forms and definition of doublespeak can help us distinguish between the reality and
what someone wants us to perceive.

sequenced pictures and using comparatives and/or superlatives.

metalanguage like “past simple”. B1 is used in Example 2 in that the students asks a question about
the right way of saying dates such as “December THE eighteenth” or “The eighteenth of December”.

2점: realia

(채점기준)

1점: (fluency)

1점:  내용의  전달과  속도

1점: (complexity)

1점: clauses와  다양한  동사  사용

(모범답안)
Fluency and complexity are two components. As for fluency, teacher focuses on the students' natural
and  clear  delivery  of  the  content,  the  speed  of  the  talk  with  less  pauses  and  false  starts.  As  for
complexity, the uses of clauses and different verbs can be evaluated. (45 words)

9

(채점기준)

1점: (oral) talk about worries

1점:  걱정과  해결을  제시한다.

1점: (written) read and organize

1점:  글을  읽고  chart를  완성한다.

(모범답안)
For oral language achievement standard, students talk about their worries and problems. In  step 5,
students tell their worries and suggest solutions. For written language, students read a short text and
organize the content. In step 4, students read a text and complete a chart. (45 words)

10

(채점기준)

1점: ‘I am on a diet and I rarely eat cookies'

1점: fewer contractions and pronouns

2점:  분명한  문장을  제공하여  이해하기  쉽게  한다.

(모범답안)
‘I am on a diet and I rarely eat cookies' is NS's grammatical adjustment, with fewer contractions and
pronouns. With a full sentence, students can understand the meaning of  sentence more easily and
cleary. (33 words)

12

(채점기준)

1점: (dictionary X) collocation

1점:  함께  쓰이는  word partners

1점: (dictionary Y) context

1점:  어떤  상황에  사용되는가에  대한  usage

(모범답안)
In  dictionary  X,  collocation  or  word  partners  is  described. Students  acquire  what  words  the  target
word, 'shed' can occur together. In dictionary Y, context is provided in usage box. Students understand
the situation the target words can be used. (39 words)

B

1

6

2점: intra-rater (intrarater)

(채점기준)

1점: (1) grammar

1점: (2) mechanics

1점: (organization) conference에서  이해도  증가

1점: (using the checklist) training sessions  확장

(모범답안)
(1) grammar, (2) mechanics, For organization, teacher prepared conference to devide the complex
indicators  into  manageable  sentences  for  better  understanding.  To  increase  the  students'
understanding of the checklist, teacher provided students with training sessions to make them fewer
errors in revision process. (42 words)

7

(채점기준)

1점: (S1) stage 3

1점: 'is the girl kicks a ball'

1점: (S2) stage 4

1점: 'where you can see the duck'

(모범답안)
For S1, stage 3 fronting is shown, as in 'is the girl kicks a ball.' For S2, stage 4, inversion can be used,
as in 'where are the birds', but no inversion in wh-questions with auxiliaries is shown, as in 'where you
can see the duck.' (46 words)

8

(채점기준)

1점: culture capsule

1점:  두  문화의  차이점과  유사점을  비교한다.

1점: culture island

1점:  교실안의  활동으로  문화활동을  제한한다.

(모범답안)
Culture capsule and culture island are used. For culture capsule, differences and similarities between
two  cultures  of  Korea  and  UK  are  compared,  discussed,  and  written.  For  culture  island,  students

decorate culture board with pictures and posters in classroom. (38 words)

1점: integrated language skills

1점: production of specific information

(모범답안)
For item 1, information transfer and for item 2, partial dictation are used. The both techniques can
assess students' integrated language skills, listening, reading and writing. They can also assess the
students' understanding and production of specific information.
realia
In the first session, the teacher focuses on fluency as the teacher evaluates how clearly and naturally
students deliver the content, checking their speed when talking and the number of false starts and
pauses.  In  the  second  session,  the  focus  is  on  complexity  as  the  teacher  checks  the  syntactic
elaborateness  and  lexical  variety  in  students’  presentations,  looking  at  how  often  students  use
dependent and independent clauses and how many different verbs they used.
The  oral  language  achievement  standard  targeted  in  is  ‘Students  can  talk  about  their  worries  and
problems’ in that students are to tell their worries to their group members and get solutions in Step 5.
The written language achievement standard is ‘Students can read a short text about a familiar topic
and organize the content’ in that students are to read the reading text and reorganize the content using
a problem-solution chart in Step 4.
The utterance that reflects NS’s grammatical adjustment to his speech is “These days I am on a diet
and I rarely eat cookies.” The NS uses fewer contractions and pronouns, changing the contracted
form ‘I’m’ into ‘I am’ and the pronoun ‘them’ into ‘cookies’.
First, ‘collocation’ is incorporated in Dictionary X in that it provides information of word partners like
‘shed tears’ to show what other words commonly occur together with the word ‘shed’. Next, ‘context’
is incorporated in Dictionary Y in that the usage box provides information on which field the word is
used in, saying that the word ‘shed’ is mainly used in journalism
intra-rater
(1) grammar (2) mechanics / First, regarding the complicated indicators for organization, the teacher
divided the indicators into several sentences so that each indicator would assess only one aspect.
Next, since students were having trouble with using the checklist appropriately, the teacher ran training
sessions, checking if students understood the indicators in the checklist after reading them, and having
them practice using it to check errors in the sample paragraph.
First, S1 is in Stage 3 in that the student uses other-fronting to form questions, putting ‘is’ to the front
as in “Is the girl kicks a ball?” and “Is the boy flies kite?”. Next, S2 is in Stage 4 in that the student’s
questions show no inversion in wh-questions with auxiliaries as in “Where you can see the duck?” and
inversion in wh-questions with a copula ‘be’ as in “Where are the birds?”, respectively
The two instructional techniques that the teacher implements in the lesson are ‘culture island’ and
‘culture capsule’. First, the teacher prepares a culture island by displaying pictures and posters which
illustrate the greeting customs of the UK on the culture board. Next, the teacher uses a culture capsule
by having students read a short passage about greeting customs in the UK and compare the greeting
customs of Korea and the UK afterwards.
Information transfer is used in Sample Item 1 and partial dictation is used in Sample Item 2. Ms. Kang
used both the techniques in order to assess her students’ listening skills in an integrative way with
other skills such as reading and writing at the same time. In addition, the techniques allowed her to
assess the students’ ability to listen selectively and find specific information
1.conversion, 2.derivation
complement
[ə]  in  the  words,  (b)  and  (c)  can  be  deleted  in  fast  speech. The  foot  structure  in  which  a  stressed
syllable is followed by one stressless syllable is most preferred in fast speech.
The sentence (i) is grammatical, whereas the sentence (ii) is ungrammatical. A locative phrase can
move to preverbal position when the verb is intransitive as in (i), whereas locative inversion cannot
occur when the verb is transitive as in (ii).
The underlined /oʊ/ is realized as [o] in the words, (b) and (d). The revised generalization in (3) is as
follows: /oʊ/ is realized as [o] when it is close to /l/ within the same morpheme.
  The sentence (i) is ungrammatical, since the AdvP, ‘persuasively’ and CP, ‘that their offer should be
rejected’ cannot be coordinated by the conjunction ‘or’. The sentence (iii) is grammatical, since CP,
‘that he was insulted’ can be in the focus position.

/oʊ/ is realized as [o] in the words soldier and poultry. The revised generalization is that /oʊ/ is realized

(i) is ungrammatical and (iii) is grammatical. In (i), AdvP ‘persuasively’ and CP ‘that their offer should
be rejected’ cannot be conjoined since only constituents which belong to the same phrasal category
can be coordinated. In (iii), CP ‘that he was insulted’ can be in the focus position because only CPs,
not TPs, can be in the focus position of wh-cleft sentences.

11  Brain/ Just as artists produce a variety of colors with paints on the palette, the palate produces various
flavors blending bitter, sweet, salt and sour flavors which are generated by the stimuli from receptor
cells on the tongue and the olfactory sense.

Lack/  The  underlined  part  means  the  neo-Impressionists  who  emerged  in  1886  occupying  the
exhibition space and driving out impression.
Third  culture  kids  have  both  benefits  and  challenge.  As  for  the  benefits,  they  can  speak  multiple
languages because they grow up internationally. As for the challenge, they may feel isolated because
frequent moving and adaption to the new environment make it difficult to maintain relationships with
people other than their families. In conclusion, educators should help them overcome their challenges
to maximize their potential.

- The palate contributes to the chef’s creating a wide spectrum of tastes and flavors, just like the palette
does for the artist.

While Cynthia thinks of the underlined “Hound” as a breed of dogs, Felicity believes that it is the name

Lack
The underlined “the last-minute guest” refers to “the neo Impressionists.”
-  The  so-called  TCKs  or  “Third  Culture  Kids”  are  children  who  spend  at  least  three  years  in  the
formative stage of their life away from their native country. Their life in foreign cultures provides them
with both benefits and challenges. One of the most significant benefits is their exposure to linguistic
environments where they can acquire multiple languages. However, they also face challenges, among
which is the problem of isolation. The main culprit of their sense of separation is frequent changes in
residential  locations,  making  it  harder  for  them  to  adjust  to  unfamiliar  life  situations.  Therefore,
educators must assist them to make the best use of possible advantages of multi-cultural experiences
in today’s increasingly globalized environments.
-  The  globalization  of  labor  market  has  led  to  a  growing  number  of  children  who  are  thrown  into
different cultures, due to frequent changes in the locations of their parents’ employment. These ever-
expanding group of kids are called “Third Culture Kids,” or TCKs. They are not only provided with
opportunities but also confronted with challenges. One of the most important benefits is that they have
an upper hand languagewise; in some cases, they are capable of being trilingual or beyond. In contrast
to this advantage, their departure from their parents’ cultural stronghold makes them undergo a terrible
sense of isolation. In order to maximize the advantages of their nomadic existence, members of the
educational  community  should  make  efforts  to  help  them  navigate  their  way  through  challenging
situations.

The teacher focuses on fluency and complexity in each presentation session. In the first session, s/he
evaluates how students deliver the content naturally and clearly in terms of speed, pause, and false
starts.  In  the  second  session,  s/he  calculates  the  rate  of  dependent  and  independent  clauses  and
counts how many different verbs are used.
In the lesson in<B>, students can achieve one oral language achievement standard ‘talk about their
worries  and  problems’  by  sharing  their  own  worries  and  solutions  in  groups.  Also,  by  filling  in  a
problem-solution chart after reading the text, they accomplish one written language standard ‘ read a
short text about a familiar topic and organize the content’

incomprehensible utterance more comprehensible to NNS.

1.Grammar
2.Mechanics
When  the  checklist  is  not  feasible,  the  teacher  provides  two  solutions.  Firstly,  by  revising  rather
complicated  indicators  for  organization  into  simplified  several  sentences,  she/he  targets  that  each
indicator assesses a single aspect. Also, with some training sessions, she/he instructs all students to
figure out the meaning of the indicator and to utilize it correctly.
S1 belongs to the developmental stage 3, while S2 has key features of stage 4. In the conversation in
<B>, S1 shows fronting saying “is the girl kicks a ball?” and “is the boy flies kite?”. On the other hand,
S2 says “where you can see the duck?” and “where are the birds?” in <b> which reflects no inversion
in wh-questions with auxiliaries, and inversion in wh-questions with copular be, respectively.
As the first instructional technique, she/he uses ‘Culture island’ by decorating the culture board with
pictures and posters. Then, she/he chooses the second instructional technique, “Culture capsule”,
where  students  are  required  to  discuss  and  write  similarities  and  differences  of  greeting  customs
between Korea and the UK.
Ms.  Kang  uses  Information  Transfer  and  Partial  Dictation  in  Sample  Item  1  and  Sample  Item  2,
respectively. With these techniques, she wants to test students’ listening skills and other skills in an
integrative way. Also, she wants to assess students’ ability to find specific details.
The  word  is  lack.  Second,  the  underlined  part  refers  to  the  neo-impressionists  that  joined  the
movement later and edged out the impressionists.
Third Culture Kids(TCK) face their own benefits and disadvantages. Regarding the former, TCKs can
acquire more language through daily exposure in their formative, everyday lives with new language.
On  the  other  hand,  the  moving  can  create  isolation  and  problems  in  maintaining  relationships.  In
conclusion, these issues should be accommodated by educators to reap the benefits of their cross-
cultural lives with less harm.

(i) is grammatical in that the intransitive verb ‘came’ allow locative inversion. Therefore, the locative
phrase ‘out of the house’ is moved to the front of the sentence and the subject ‘an old lady’ and the
verb ‘came’ are inverted. (ii) is ungrammatical because the transitive verb ‘live’ does not allow locative
inversion.

content naturally and clearly in the first presentation. For complexity, he calculated the total of different

The teaching procedure targets at the skill that students can talk about their worries and problems for
the oral language achievement standard. In Step 5, the teacher asks the students in groups to tell their
worries and suggest solutions for each other. It also targets at the skill that student can read a short
text about a familiar topic and organize the content for the written language language achievement
standard. For this, in Step 4, the teacher asks the students to read the text one more time to complete
a problem-solution chart based on what they read
The utterance that reflects NS’s grammatical adjustment to his speech is the following: These days I
am on a diet and I rarely eat cookies. This utterance  uses fewer contractions and pronouns for its
adjustment. NS said “I am” for “I’m” to reduce the contractions and used “cookies” in stead of “them”
to avoid the use of pronouns in his speech directed toward NNS.
brain. Just as the palette is integral part of a painting process, the palate is the primary place that

First, the collocation feature is applied in Dictionary X. The word partners in the box in Dictionary X
shows the lists of the words that could co-occur with the target word, ‘shed’, such as “jobs”, “weight”,
and many more. Second, the context feature is applied in Dictionary Y. The usage box provides L2
learners with the information that the target word, ‘shed’, is primarily used in journalism in the real
world context.

(i) is ungrammatical because the adverb phrase ‘persuasively’ and the CP ‘that their offer should be

The right word for each blank in (1) and (2)  is grammar and mechanics, respectively. To solve the
problems the teacher experienced using the checklist, the teacher first separated the indicators for
organization in writing into two or three sentences to make each indicator assesses one aspect at a
time. Second, the teacher read out the indicators for the students during the training sessions and
asked  the  students  to  use  them  to  check  the  errors  in  the  given  sample  paragraph  the  teacher
prepared for them.
S1 is in Stage 3 because S1 uttered “Is the girl kicks a ball?” and “Is the boy flies kite?” to make a
question. S2 is in Stage 4 because S2 uttered “Where you can see the duck?” and “Where are the
birds?” to make a question formation
The culture island technique was applied when the teacher decorated the culture board with posters
and pictures illustrating the ways people greet each other in the UK and asked the students to check
them out to tell each other what they think about the posters and pictures. The culture capsule was
also applied when a short passage concerning greeting customs in the UK was prepared in advance
and read out by the teacher to have students to take notes. Then the teacher has the students discuss
and write the similarities and differences between the UK and Korea in terms of the greeting customs.
Sample  Item  1  and  2  used  ‘information  transfer’  and  ‘partial  dictation’  as  the  item  techniques,
respectively. Ms. Kang used these techniques to measure how students could integrate their listening
abilities with other language skills all at the same time and how they could find specific information.
lack. The underlined part means the neo-Impressionists who were born from Impressionism and who
were edging out Impressionism itself.
The children who live their lives as Third Culture Kids experience both challenges and advantages.
These  kids  become  the  users  of  multiple  languages  as  they  are  exposed  to  various  languages  in
schools and daily lives. However, constant re-locations from one place to another make it difficult for
them  to  adjust  to  new  life  and  develop  social  relationships,  which  gives  them  a  sense  of  isolation.
Educators should make their efforts to maximize the benefits of their cross-cultural experiences while
minimizing the challenges they would face in their lives.

(모범답안)  The  two  words  are  ‘chocolate’  and  ‘nationalize’.  /  The  most  preferred  foot  structure  is
stressed-stressless. To be specific, the sequence of stressed syllables is not allowed as in the blockage
of schwa deletion. Also, the stressless syllable follows the stressed syllable, not vice versa.

(채점기준)  1점:  (i)이  비문임을  식별.  1점:  (iv)가  비문임을  식별.  1점:  (i)이  비문이  되는  이유는

병렬구조를  이루고  있는  AdvP와  CP가  같은  범주가  아니기  때문임  1점:  (iv)가  비문이  되는

이유는  believe  유형인  intend  구문에서  pseudo-cleft  촛점  위치에  TP가  올  수  없기  때문임

(모범답안)  The  sentences  (i)  and  (iv)  are  ungrammatical.  In  the  case  of  (i),  as  AdvP  and  a  CP  are
wrongly coordinated because they do not belong to the same category. As for (iv), a TP cannot occur
in the focus position of the pseudo-cleft in the case of ‘intend’ construction.

(채점기준)  1.5점:  빈  칸을  lack으로  기입  2.5점:  밑줄  친  부분의  의미는  neo-Impressionists임을

There are both benefits and challenges of being a third culture kid. As for benefits, third culture kids
can develop the ability to speak multiple languages as they are exposed to the language frequently in
everyday  life.  However,  they  might  suffer  from  an  undeniable  challenge  as  they  have  to  move  and
adjust to new life circumstances, which makes them feel a sense of isolation. In conclusion, educators
should  help  them  to  maximize  benefits  of  crosscultural  experiences  while  guiding  them  to  handle
challenges.

Two words where [ə] can be deleted in fast speech are b. ‘chocolate’ and c. ‘nationalize.’ The foot
structure of ‘chocolate’ is [ˈtʃaklɪt] as [ə] in a medial stressless syllable is deleted after a stressed and
before a stressless syllable. The foot structure of ‘nationalize’ is [ˈnæ ʃənˌlaɪz] or [ˈnæ ʃnəˌlaɪz] as [ə]
in  either  stressless  syllable  is  deleted  since  two  stressless  syllables  occur  between  two  stressed
syllables. (-1?  디렉션  잘못  파악하는  실수  저지름)
(i) is grammatical while (ii) is ungrammatical. In (i), the verb, ‘came’ is intransitive, so the locative
phrase ‘out of the house’ can be moved to the front of the sentence and the verb ‘came’ and the
subject ‘an old lady’ are inverted. In (ii), the verb, ‘lived’ is transitive, so the locative phrase ‘under the
bridge’ cannot be moved to the front of the sentence and the verb ‘lived’ and the subject ‘a troll’
cannot be inverted because the subject ‘a troll’ and the complement ‘a good life’ cannot be next to
each other
In the first presentation, the teacher focuses on fluency. The teacher evaluated students’
presentations based on their speed of the talk and how many pauses and false starts occurred,
focusing on how clearly and naturally the content is delivered. In the second presentation, the
teacher focuses on complexity. It was evaluated by tallying the number of verbs that are used
differently and calculating the ratio of dependent and independent clauses

First, the teacher implements Culture island. The teacher decorated the culture board in the English
classroom with pictures and posters which illustrate the greeting customs of the UK, and the students
told their thoughts about the pictures and posters. Second, the teacher implements Culture capsule.
The  teacher  read  a  short  passage  about  greeting  customs  in  the  UK,  and  after  taking  notes,  the
students discussed and wrote the similarities and differences of the greeting customs between Korea
and the UK.

could find and understand specific details.

To live as a ‘Third Culture Kids’(TCKs) can give benefits and undeniable challenges to the children
raised outside the parents’ home cultures. First, in terms of benefits, TCKs can become speakers of
multiple language by attending schools in the target language and encountering the language in life
every day, though the fluency level can vary. On the other hand, there is an undeniable challenge

circumstances, preventing them from maintaining relationships with people outside their immediate
family. In conclusion, educators should maximize the benefits of cross-cultural experiences and help
TCKs deal with challenges for global education.

Sentence (i) is grammatical, while sentence (ii) is ungrammatical. Sentence (i) is grammatical because
the verb “came” and the subject “an old lady” are correctly inverted after preposing the locative PP
“out  of  the  house”;  there  is  no  object  NP  subcategorized  by  the  verb  “came”.  Sentence  (ii)  is

locative PP “under the bridge” violating the restriction on locative inversion.(-2)
In the first session, the teacher focuses on “fluency”. The teacher examines how the students deliver

all relate to students’ fluency. In the second session, “complexity” is focused. The teacher’s identifying
variety  of  verbs  and  use  of  different  clause  types  is  closely  related  to  “complexity”  of  students’

they have read in the reading text.

Life of a TCK, a Third Culture Kid, have both a benefit and a challenge. TCKs become a competent
multilingual  as  they  are  exposed  to  different  languages  of  different  cultures  in  everyday  situations.

unable  to  build  intimate  relations  with  people  other  than  family  members.  To  conclude,  educators
should consider ways to maximize the benefits TCKs have as well as ways to cope with challenges

Living as third culture kids have benefits and challenges. First, TCKs can learn multi languages fast
and easily thanks to daily exposure to them, Schools teach in the target language, and students mee
the language in everyday life. Second, TCKs experience isolation due to multiple migration in location
and having to adjust to new life environments. This impedes their maintaining relationships with other
people  outside  their  family.  In  conclusion,  educators  shoud  support  TCKs  maximize  their  potential
benefits of international experiences and navigate the disadvantages.

 The sentence (i) has an embedded reading, since the negation ‘not’ that is in the embedded clause
c-commands the NPI ‘any’, which means that ‘in any room’ modifies the embedded predicate. The
sentence  (ii)  has  both  readings  since  the  negation  can  c-command  the  NPI  ‘any’  regardless  of  its
position, which means that the adverbial can modify both matrix and embedded predicates.
In (i) ‘did you’, palatalization is involved. The alveolar stop /d/ is palatalized when it is followed by the
palatal  approximant  /j/.  In  (ii),  the  spelling  pronunciation  error is  found,  which  is  based  on
the   misunderstanding that the final sound of the word 'fleas' would be pronunciated [s] rather than [z]
as it is spelled.
Specifier
Assimilation and dissimilation are involved in the data in (1) and (2), respectively. In (2), A suffix that
has  the  [-lateral]  feature  like  ‘-ar’  is  attached  to  the  base  whose  final  consonant  has  the  [+lateral]
feature, whereas a suffix of the [+lateral] like ‘-al’ is attached to the base whose final consonant has the
[-lateral].
‘married’ in (i) is a verb, whereas ‘married in (ii) is an adjective. The adjective ’married’ in (ii) cannot be
modified by a degree modifier as in ‘*They were very married until last Christmas.’ since it is a non-
gradable adjective. However, it can be used after the verb ‘remain’ as in ‘They remained married until
last Christmas.’
affricate
(i) has an embedded reading and (ii) has both readings. In (i), in any room must modify (did not) sing
in order for not to c-command any. In (ii), whether in any room modifies (did not) say or sang, not c-
commands any
Palatalization can be applied to (i). In a connected speech, the alveolar stop /d/ becomes /ʤ/ before a
palatal glide /j/. Spelling pronunciation is shown in (ii). S1 thinks that the pronunciation of fleas is [flis]
influenced by the spelling ‘s’, rather than the correct pronunciation [fliz]
specifier
(1) assimilation (2) dissimilation. The allomorph -al occurs when the base ends with a consonant with
[–lateral], and -ar occurs when the base ends with a consonant with [+lateral].

embedded predicate ‘sing’ because the NPI ‘any’ must be c-commanded by the negation ‘not’.

‘not’.) (ii) has both readings. The adverbial ‘in any room’ can modify either the matrix
predicate ‘say’ or the embedded predicate ‘sang’ because sentence (ii) observes the
c-command condition in both readings

In <B>, “cataphoric words” and “back channel cues(-1)” are used. As for the former, it is shown in
“Oh, wait, on her jacket, I found this. There is a letter P on it.” Here, “this” refers to “a letter P on it”,
which is mentioned later than “this”. In the case of the latter, it is shown in “I also see a P on her
jacket in my picture.” Here, S2 uses a back channel cue by showing that S2 understands S1
properly. (-1)
(i) has the embedded reading, whereas (ii) has both readings. In the case of (i), the adverbial “in any
room” can only modify the embedded element “sing” because the NPI “any” should be ccommanded
by “not”. As for (ii), the adverbial “in any room” can modify either “say” or “sang” because “any” can
be c-commanded by “not” in both cases

Ver.1) n (ii), the extraposed CP is adjoined to TP. The preposing in (iii) is ungrammatical because it
violates a binding condition (binding principle B). The only binding (c-commanding) antecedent of himi
in (iii) is Johni and then the correct form must be himself.

Ver.2) In (ii), the extraposed CP is adjoined to TP. The preposing in (iii) is ungrammatical because only
phrasal constituents can move, but the moved ‘Work with John who knew him’ does not form a phrasal
constituent. The extraposed CP ‘who knew him’ is adjoined to TP, so it cannot form a phrase with the
VP ‘work with John,'

Interference occurs in “No, I eat them everyday” and “Yes, I never eat them”. They are interference in
that  the  transfer  occurs  interlingually.  When  Koreans  are  asked  whether  they  like  something  in  a
negative question in Korean, the answer can include both negative and positive elements as in the two
answers, which is the opposite in English.

Two attributive-only adjectives are ‘absolute’ and ‘urban’. ‘Absolute’ belongs to Adjectives of Degree,
and ‘urban’ belongs to Associative Adjectives.
In some AE varieties, dark ‘l’ occurs (in onsets) before front vowels; darker ‘l’ appears (in onsets) before
back  vowels.  In  AAVE,  vocalization  of  /l/  occurs  in  codas  before  nonlabials  (velars  or  alveolars)  or
without any following consonant. The deletion of /l/ takes place in codas before labials.

by letting others do the job as a policeman.
The  student  used  avoidance,  appeal  to  authority,  and  word  coinage  for  the  following  reasons,
respectively.  First,  he  used  active  sentences  to  avoid  using  passive  ones  with  the  ‘bicycle’  as  the
subject. Next, he looked up the word ‘manufacture’ in a dictionary to substitute ‘make’. Third, he made
up a non-existing word ‘four-cycle’ based on the supposed rule of adding ‘four’ in front of ‘cycle’.
The word is ‘peace.’ First, inanimate objects break down generating inconvenience and frustration to
man. Secondly, for those of inability to break down, they get lost in mystery. The last of their kinds
never work again after the first operation.
PRO in (ia) and (ib) are non-arbitrary and arbitrary, respectively. PRO in (ia) is obligatory control. In (ii),
(a) and (c) are control constructions. (a) is object control and (c) is subject control.
Melatonin proves to keep the brain in order in two ways. As an antidepressant, low doses of melatonin
relieve seasonal depression common in winter by rearranging the disordered sleep-wake due to the
changing light-dark cycle. Also, melatonin supplements can alleviate age-related cognitive decline like
Alzheimer’s disease by fighting against its causes, toxic amyloid beta and tau proteins. To conclude,

The type of negative transfer in B is interference. The first example is “No, I eat them everyday.” The
second  example  is  “Yes,  I  never  eat  them.”  The  reason  is  regarding  that  the  transfer  occurs
interlingually,  as  follows:  In  the  Korean  language,  the  answer  starts  with  “Yes,”  if  the  question  is
affirmative and the answer is affirmative and if the question is negative and the answer is negative. The
answer starts with “No,” if the question is affirmative and the answer is negative and if the question is
negative and the answer is affirmative. However, in English, the answer starts with “Yes” if the answer
is affirmative and the answer starts with “No” if the answer is negative regardless of the question type.

genenral general scale and overall impressions.

  First, the extraposed CP in (ii), derived from (i), is adjoined to ‘TP’. Second, the preposing in (iii),
derived from (ii) is ungrammatical. Since the extraposed CP ‘who knew him’ from the Subject position
is adjoined to TP and only phrasal constituents can move, the VP ‘work with John’ cannot be preposed

The type of negative transfer in <B> is interference. The following two examples show interference:
“No, I eat them everyday. They are good for my health.” and “Yes, I never eat them. But I like
mangos.” They exemplify interference because transfer occurs interlingually from Korean to English.
Specifically, in Korean, people reply to negative questions based on the negative word itself, as “No”
when they do the opposite and as “Yes” when they do the thing in the question. Thus, Korean
learners tend to apply this rule when responding to negative questions in English.

general scale, not the analytic scoring with five criteria suggested for helpful information to students.
Second, it is because the teacher conducted the speaking test not to determine students’ current
levels and place them into appropriate courses, which is the placement test, but in order to check
the students’ aptitude in English based on their potential strengths, which is the aptitude test.

First, the extraposed CP in (i) is adjoined to TP. Second, the preposing in (iii) is ungrammatical because

10  Step 4 is not related to task based language teaching. The synthetic syllabus is to teach discrete point
items separately. However, TBLT should be based on analytic syllabus, where language is taught as a
meaningful whole rather than isolated structure. With the students’ performance of target tasks, the
language is analyzed and practiced in contexts.
diagnostic, The test was administered to check the student’s readiness and strengths and weaknesses
before the class. The teacher has a chance to provide more personal and clear guide to improve the
student’s specific difficulty of vocabulary memorization before the class.
Activity 3 provides the students with communicative activity using the target form. The students begin
with generating their own ideas related to authentic situation. They use the target structure to share
their  ideas  to  each  other  in  a  meaningful  interaction.  They  are  more  interested  and  motivated  to
negotiate meaning in an authentic context of interview.
Ms. Shin’s class conforms to the two parts, objective and communication strategies according to the
senior  teacher’s  suggestions. The  students  practice  making  a  function,  request  using  the  question
forms  to  complete  the  task  of  collecting  the  information  in  the  book  order  form.  They  also  have  a
chance  to  use  communication  strategies,  approximation  or  body  language  for  the  communication
difficulty.
In contrast, Ms. Shin’s class does not follow the other two factors, global error correction and implicit
feedback. Even though the senior teacher advises that the teacher focus on global errors, she just
corrects a local language error, verb + ‘s’ after the  third person singular. This local error does not
interfere the meaning of communication when the language error is made. Accordingly, the teacher
gives explicit negative feedback, explicit correction with a revised answer using some metalinguistic
terms on the local error.

[해설] (6), (7), (5)번을  위와  같이  적지  않고  답안을  쓰면  충분히  4줄  안에  쓸  수  있음.
Museums have socially changed in their purpose and role. First, museums have changed collecting
purpose from extraordinary materials of the past to the ordinary ones that show many people's lives,
which increases their relevance to and interest of people. Second, museums has begun to play an
important role in the contemporary life. They are expanding their interaction with social sectors beyond

Ms. Shin’s class conforms to the suggestions on Objective and Strategy. First, she focuses on language
function rather than grammatical structures. It is because she guides students to practice the function
of making requests by asking for information in pairs using a book order form. Second, she facilitates
the use of communication strategies. It is because she encourages students to try using similar words
or gestures, which are an approximation strategy and a kind of nonlinguistic signals respectively.
  However, Ms. Shin’s class does not conform to the suggestions on Error targeted and Feedback. First,
she focuses on local errors, not global errors. It is because she offers the feedback on the third person
singular present marker ‘-s’, which does not impede communication of meaning. Second, she provides
explicit feedback, not implicit one. It is because she uses ‘explicit correction’ by indicating the error
and providing the correct form such as “comes” instead of using an implicit and unobtrusive one like
‘recast’.

The insertion of glides /j/ and /w/ occurs between two vowels where the preceding vowels should be
a high vowels or a dipthong ending in a high vowel.
The glide /j/ is inserted when the preceding vowel is a high front vowel or a dipthong ending in a high
front vowel, whereas the glide /w/ is inserted when the  preceding vowel is a high back vowel or a
dipthong ending in a high back vowel.

help  you  until  you  will  finish  it.'  In  adverbial  time  clause,  the  simple  present  tense  should  be  used
instead of 'will' to express future time.

bound, and the NP 'Tom' moves into the subject position of the middle clause and then into the matrix
subject position without crossing any subject.

12  Sentence (4) and sentence (5) can be conjoined with the coordinate conjunction but as in sentence
(6). Sentence (4) has the status of CP because main clauses lacking an overt complementizer are CP
constituents.  Sentence  (5)  has  also  the  status  of  CP  because main clauses  containing  an  inverted
auxiliary (here should ) are CP constituents. Therefore, the given two sentences can be conjoined
because they belong to the same grammatical category, CP.

A glide is inserted between two vowels when the first is a high vowel or a diphthong. The palatal glide
/j/ is inserted between the two vowels when the preceding vowel is a high front vowel or a diphthong
ending with a high front vowel, /ɑɪ/. The velar glide /w/ is inserted when the preceding vowel is a high
back vowel or a diphthong ending with a high back vowel, /ɑʊ/ or /oʊ/.

Sentence  (5)  in  <B>  is  syntactically  well-formed.  The  matrix  subject  Tom  originates  in  the  subject
position of the lowest embedded clause and is assigned a theta role by the verb phrase brag about
himself . In this position, the reflexive pronoun (or the anaphor) himself can be bound by its antecedent
Tom in its binding domain, the smallest clause; thus, it does not violate the binding condition. Then
Tom in the subject of the lowest embedded clause moves to the matrix subject position. This movement
does not violate any movement constraint because Tom does not cross any subject.

Museums have recently transformed their aims and functions in society. First, museums now collect
more ordinary objects instead of special or rare items to better portray common living in the past. In
addition to this, museums have begun to partner with allies(sectors) beyond the narrow educational
sphere, reaching out to political, business, and community institutes. Through these changes, modern
museums have adapted themselves to be a crucial part of contemporary culture.

According  to  <B>,  Ms.  Shin  conforms  to  two  suggestions  from  the  senior  teacher:  focusing  on
language  functions  and  encouraging  the  use  of  communication  strategies.  First,  Ms.  Shin  makes
students practice making requests during the lesson, which is one of the language functions. Also, she
mentions that the next class will deal with asking for permission which is another language function.
Next, Ms. Shin asks students to use similar words or gestures when the exact words do not come to
their minds during the activity. That is, as the suggestion of the senior teacher, she encourages them
to use communication strategies such as approximation or nonlinguistic signals.
On the other hand, Ms. Shin deviates from the other two suggestions made by the senior teacher:
focusing only on global errors and implicit correction. In <B>, Ms. Shin point outs the grammatical
error which does not hinder the communication of meaning. Furthermore, Ms. Shin explicitly corrects
points out the erroneous point in the students’ utterances, which is a missing ‘s’ needed for singular
third person verbs. Thus, she does not comply with the suggestions to focus only on global errors and
to provide implicit correction.

Kim’s test is to provide the diagnostic information on students’ strengths and weakness to see how
