it evokes students’ interests in learning and promotes meaningful and active interaction among
themselves when they are led to interview each other about his or her feelings about the
accomplishment of their dream jobs by taking turns as a reporter.

13  Ms. Shin’s class conforms to the senior teacher’s suggestions in terms of objective and strategy. First,
today’s lesson centers on making requests with opportunities to use the question forms. Second, the
teacher  encourages  students  to  use  communication  strategies  by  using  similar  words  or  gestures
when the can’t find the right words to express the meaning they want to come across.

The teacher’s class, however, does not conform to the suggestions with regard to error targeted and
feedback. First, the teacher treated the error related to missing ‘-s’ for some verbs like ‘he come’ while
the meaning was still clear to each other. Second, she treat the students’ errors explicitly rather than
implicitly when she told the students that they should put –s at the end of the verb, ‘come’.

When negation has wide scope over quantifier, it can be paraphrased as “Mary visited no city that Tom
visited.” (“Mary did not visit any city -”) By contrast, when quantifier has wide scope over negation, it
can be paraphrased as “Mary visited some cities that Tom visited, but she did not visit other cities that
Tom visited.” With these two reading, sentence (6) can be ambiguous.
The narrator employs ‘short men’ instead of ‘little boys’ because the children here already learned the
violence of adulthood. For example, they say they will easily kill younger ones. They also imitate the
behaviors of adults, clearing throats, making faces, etc. The blank is filled with ‘playing war’. All these
show improper examples of rite of passage for children.
The coordination presented in (6) is not permitted because they belong to different categories. (4)
shows an example of TP as explained in the passage. By contrast, (6) shows a CP because the modal
‘should’ occupies the CP-spec position through inversion. Thus, CP and TP cannot be coordinated.
The participants in the two groups are characterized as in the following: one group drinks daily and

collect  samples  by  random.  It  was  not  determined  randomly  which  people  would  belong  to  which
group, and nondrinking people already had health problems.
Between vowels, when the preceding vowel is stressed, a glide sharing the articulation place with it
can be inserted. On /j/-insertion, when the preceding vowel is front and stressed, /j/ is inserted. About
/w/-insertion, when the preceding vowel is back and stressed, /w/ is inserted. But, as in (3), when the
glide does not share the place of articulation, such insertions do not occur.

city (that Tom visited).

didn’t visit. On the other hand, when refused has a wide scope over every city (that Tom visited), the
meaning of the sentence (3) is that Mary visited some of the cities that Tom visited.

When tense vowels such as a high front tense vowel, a high back tense vowel, and a diphthong are
followed  by  a  vowel,  a  glide  is  inserted.  /j/  is  inserted  when  a  word  or  a  syllable  ending  in  /i/  or  a
diphthong  which  finishes  with  /ɪ/  is  followed  by  a  vowel.  /w/  is  inserted  when  a  word  or  a  syllable
ending in /u/, or a diphthong which finishes with /ʊ/ is followed by a vowel.

The sentence (5) in <B> is syntactically well-formed. The reason is that if we assume that the deep
structure of the sentence (5) is like the following sentence, It appears to Mary that his friends believes
Tom to brag about himself, we can notice that Tom in (5) can be assigned a theta role by the following
verb brag and the sentence (5) does not violate the movement constraint which bans a subject from
crossing another subject, and the anaphor himself can be bound by the antecedent Tom because they
are in the same clause.
Museums’ purpose and role in society are changed in last few decades. First, the purpose of museums’
collection  is  reevaluated,  and  they  put  a  lot  of  effort  into  collecting  the  everyday  and  ordinary
collections.  For  a  new  role  in  society,  they  make  partnerships  with  all  sectors  of  society  including
business  and  community  sectors  and  political  associations.  To  become  a  center  of  contemporary
culture, the museums should reinvent themselves in these ways.
The  two  suggestions  Ms.  Shin's  class  takes  up  are  as  follows:  'Objective'  and  'Strategy'  parts.
Concerning the former, the teacher focuses on teaching a language function while having her students
in  pairs  complete  a  book  order  form.  To  fill  in  the  form,  students  need  to  make  requests  for  the
necessary  information  from  the  partner.  As  for  the  latter,  she  facilitates  the  students  to  use
communication strategies such as approximation and body languages when they fail to think of some
words in English during the pair work.
On the other hand, Ms. Shin's class does not conform to the senior teacher's advice specifically for
'Error targeted' and 'Feedback.' First of all, unlike the suggestion of giving feedback only on global
errors, a local error is pointed out. For example, the teacher revises a subject-verb agreement error
which did not hinder communication. Besides, given that the way the error is corrected is explicit, the
class does not follow the suggestion of providing correction implicitly.

The sentence (4) and (5) can be conjoined. The coordinate conjunctions can conjoin constituents of
the same grammatical category but cannot conjoin constituents of different grammatical categories.
Thus, conjunction 'but' can be conjoin sentence 4 and 5, which are all TP. (-2)

The generalization for glide insertion is intervocalic position followed by high vowels. The condition
for /j/ insertion is that /j/ comes before high front vowels. The condition for /w/ insertion is that /w/
comes before high back vowels.

  First meaning is as follows: It was every city that Tom visited that Mary refused to visit. In this case, a
quantifier ‘every city’ has a wide scope over a negative expression ‘refuse.’ Second meaning is as
follows: Mary agreed to visit some cities that Tom visited, but refused to visit some cities that Tom
visited. In this case, the negative expression ‘refuse’ has a wide scope over the quantifier ‘every city.

  Two ungrammatical sentences are as follows: ‘I’ll be excited when the conference will begin.’ and ‘I’ll
help you until you will finish it.’ The reason is that when ‘will’ expresses future time in adverbial time
clause, it should be used in the simple present tense.
Activity  3  is  the  most  appropriate  activity.  The  reason  is  that  it  involves  students  in  authentic

The sentence 5 is syntactically well-formed. The reasons are as follows: firstly, Tom is assigned a theta
role by the verb ‘brag.’ Second, it does not  violate any movement constraints. Thirdly, the anaphor
‘himself’ is bound by its antecedent ‘Tom’ in its binding domain. (-2)
Museums have reformed their purpose and role. In terms of purpose, they make an effort to collect
the everyday materials to represent the real life of most people. And in terms of role, they make some
partnership  with  other  political,  business,  and  community  sectors  in  order  to  place  themselves  in
mainstream  contemporary  life.  By  doing  so,  they  reinvent  themselves  as  the  true  center  of
contemporary culture. (-2)
Two suggestions that Ms. Shin’s class conforms are the objective and the strategy. Firstly, her
class  centers  on  one  language  function  which  is  making  request  by  doing  book  ordering  activity.
Secondly, her class encourages the use of communication strategies. For example, she encourages
students to use the similar words or gestures.
Two suggestions that Ms. Shin’s class does not conform are error correction and feedback part. Firstly,
she focuses even on local error. For example, she corrects the error of incorrect use of third person
singular  ’comes’  even  though  the  meaning  is  still  clear  without  ‘s.’  Secondly,  she  gives  explicit
feedback by saying “It should be “comes” not “come”.” (-2)

The first reading is that Mary didn’t want to visit any city that Tom visited, and the second reading is
that Mary wanted to visit not all of the cities that Tom visited but possibly wanted to visit some of them.

Tom visited’ and ‘every city Tom visited’ can have a wide scope over ‘refused’. (-2)

12  Sentence (4) and (5) cannot be conjoined into sentence (6). Sentence (4) is a TP which doesn’t have
a complementiser while sentence (5) is a CP that has ‘should’ in the place of complementiser. As they
have different categories, they cannot be conjoined (-4)
‘diagnostic’ best fits the blank. The teacher took a test before the class starts, so that she can diagnose
student’s starting points, strengths, and weaknesses and reflect them to the class.
The participants in the drinking groups have usually had one drink daily, while some of the people in
the nondrinking groups have abstained from drinking due to their possible medical problems. Those
experiments  are  flawed  in  design,  as  it  didn’t  apply  ‘random  assignment’  which  can  lead  to  true
comparison without being affected by other variables such as medical history of the subjects. As they
didn’t control those variables, the experiments are problematic.
A glide is inserted between two heterosyllabic vowels, first of which being a front vowel. When the
preceding vowel is a high front vowel and is followed by another vowel, the palatal glide /j/ is inserted.
When the preceding vowel is a back front vowel and is followed by another vowel, /w/ is inserted. (-1)
Ashbury thinks that his mother might not immediately understand the message because his mother
has a ‘literal mind’, which means that she tends to understand a text not figuratively but literally in the
surface level. ‘domesticated’ best fits the blank.
‘pipe’s location’ best fits the blank. The two factors are the records of the actual pipe’s location and
those of the drowser’s guesses. If the two factors correspond to each other, the guess is regarded as
a correct guess.
  The Man’s utterances “I’ll be excited when the conference will begin” and “I’ll help you until you will
finish  it”  contain  incorrect  usages  of  ‘will’.  The  subordinate  clauses  in  these  sentences  are  time
adverbial clauses, so the present tense must be used instead of ‘will’ to express future time. Therefore,
‘when the conference will begin’ and ‘until you will finish it’ are ungrammatical.
Activity 3 is the most appropriate one that reflects Ms. Lee’s opinions. In activity 3, students are invited
to use the target structure “If I were” to express what they want to say, which means they are engaging
in  the  communication  with  a  real  purpose.  While  talking  about  their  dreams  as  a  reporter  and  an
interviewee, students naturally use the target form with communicative purpose.
Sentence (5) is syntactically well-formed. The matrix clause ‘Tom’ assigned the theta role from the
verb ‘brag’, and it does not violate any movement constraint. Plus, the anaphor “himself” can be bound,
as the trace of “Tom” is within the clause containing the anaphor. Thus, sentence (5) is grammatical.
(-2)
Beyond their reputations of mere culture repositories, museums have been changing their purpose
and role recently. First, they started to collect and display the ordinary collections of common people,
sheding new lights on the ordinary lives of people. Second, they try to permeated to wider aspects of
our  lives  by  building  partnerships  with  educational,  political,  and  business  associations.  By  these
changes, museums are becoming an essential part of contemporary changes.
Ms. Shin’s class conforms to the two suggestions in terms of ‘objective’ and ‘strategy’. First, the teacher
clearly informs students that they are focusing on ‘how to make request’, which is a communicative
function rather than a grammatical structure. By doing so, students can understand that their primary
focus is on the communicative function and the grammatical forms get the secondary focus. Second,
the teacher encourages students to use communication strategies such as approximation and making
gestures.  This  can  lead  (?)  students  to  solve  the  communication  problem  on  their  own  using  the
strategies.
However,  Ms.  Shin’s  class  does  not  conform  to  the  suggestions  in  two  parts:  ‘Error  targeted’  and
‘Feedback’. The teacher points out the incorrect use of the inflectional suffix ‘-s’ even though it is a
local error. Moreover, she gives an explicit correction as feedback, mentioning the correct form of the
error. This can be seen in her saying ‘It should be “comes” not “come”…’ To sum up, Ms shin’s class
does not conform to the suggestions in indicating and correcting the error in the class.

13  Sound, Reading should be understood to comprehend the whole context through topdown reading
approach rather than just decoding isolated sounds. Language should be taught as a whole not just
focusing on isolated and discrete features of language.
Mr.  Song  implements  focus  on  forms  approach  to  focus  on  the  grammatical  structures  without
contexts. He explicitly presents the rules with metalinguistic terms and cannot give intrinsic motivation
to  involve  the  learning.  In  contrast,  Ms.  Oh  implements  focus  on  form  approach  using  input
enhancement in contexts. Students implicitly notice the target structure in the reading passage.
The material is adapted to personalize to learners’ low proficiency levels and their interests in sports.
The  techniques  Mr.  Lee  uses  are  adding  and  reordering.  By  increasing  the  prewriting  activities,
students can have more opportunities to generate their own ideas. By reordering texts, students are
more prepared to engage in writing activity.
Minji used clarification request, ‘…repeat what you said’ and comprehensible check, ‘…know what I
mean?’  Hyerim  used  comprehension  check,  ‘…you  understand?’  to  negotiate  meaning  during
conversational interaction.

The sentences (iii) and (v) are the sentences containing an unaccusative verb. The reason is that the
verb remain in (iii) and the verb arise in (v) allow a word order called there inversion, as is evidenced
in the following grammatical sentences: (iii) There remained several students in the school library. (v)
There arose several complications in the medical experiment.

 Mr. Song follows a focus on forms approach because he teaches the number of grammatical rules
explicitly  by  using  meta-linguistic  terms.  Miss  Oh,  however,  implements  a  form-focused  instruction
according  to  a  focus  on  form  approach  because  she  attempts  to  help  students  to  understand  the
function  of  the  target  structures  by  making  them  italicized  and  has  the  students  check  their
understanding with their group members.
Mr. Lee adapts his materials to localize them because the textbook in the writing section is too difficult
for  his  low-ability  students.  Also,  he  does  so  to  personalize  the  materials  since  sports  are  more
appealing and relevant to his students. For his materials adaptation, he is going to utilize adding and
reordering.
Schwa  deletion  occurs  when  the  syllable  containing  a  schwa  is  preceded  by  the  stressed  syllable
containing a stressed vowel and followed by the unstressed syllable containing another schwa.
Mijin used a clarification request when she said “I’m sorry?” and a comprehension check by saying
“You know what I mean?” Haerim also used a comprehension check as her meaning-negotiation
strategy when she said, “Do you understand?”

The (3) associative use best accounts for the use of two definite articles in <B>. The reason is that
since the word taxi is usually associated with the words driver and passenger, the speaker can
assume that the listener knows about the relationship that exist between an object, a taxi, and
persons, the driver and the passengers

As multitasking becomes useful and advantageous, some challenges began to emerge. First, there is
fatal  danger  of  using  electronic  devices  and  driving  at  the  same  time..  Next,  multitasking  in  the
workplace can decrease productivity. Moreover, it negatively influences how we learn. Thus, we should
challenge the assumption that multitasking is better.

The teacher in Class A plays the role of a facilitator. For example, the teacher guides the students’
consensus building activity by offering his help and feedback as needed. The teacher in Class B,
however, plays the role of a controller. For example, the teacher first explains the grammatical form
of comparatives and then tightly controls the students’ language by asking them to listen to the
recording line-by-line and then repeat them.
To manage the classroom, the teacher in Class A walks around the classroom to encourage
students to participate in the discussion if they are reluctant to jin in the group work. The teacher in
Class B, however, stays at the front of the class the entire time
and plays the recording repeatedly for choral repetition.

Schwa  deletion  occurs  (in  fast  speech)  when  the  following  syllable  has  another  schwa  and  the
preceding syllable[vowel] is stressed.
The associative use in (3) best accounts for the use of the two definite articles in <B>. The speaker
can safely assume that the listener knows that the driver and the passengers are associated with the
taxi in the accident and they were riding in the taxi.

(4) can account for the ungrammaticality of sentence (ii). If we assume the binary branching structure
in  (4),  the  antecedent  the  boys  cannot  c-command  the  anaphor  each  other  in  (ii),  making  it
ungrammatical. If we accept the ternary branching structure in (3), the boys c-commands each other
in (ii), thereby making it grammatical, which is not the case.

The most appropriate word for the blank is ‘imitation.’ Manufacturers started to use ‘distinctive names’
to avoid the law, the Pure Food and Drug Act of 1906 that prohibits mislabeling, labelling something
as a certain food for an imitated one. Under this law, they could sell imitated products to consumers
with impunity.
Multitasking,  doing  many  demands  at  once,  is  assumed  to  be  a  useful  strategy,  but  there  emerge
counter evidence against it. For example, driving while using electronic devices leads to a fatal danger.
Also, multitasking decreases problem solving capabilities of workers. Moreover, multitasking harms
our  learning  capability  by  making  information  processing  fragmented  and  less  flexible.  Thus,  the
assumption that multitasking is beneficial should be challenged.

(3) associative use
In the sentence, the driver and the passenger are associated with the taxi the speaker mentions in
relation  to  the  accident.  The  speaker  thinks  that  the  listener  understands  such  association  or

For  (i)  to  be  grammatical,  the  anaphor  each  other  (direct  object)  must  be  c-commanded  by  its
antecedent the boys (indirect object) that is co-indexed with it. In structure (4), the indirect object c-
commands the direct object and thus the former properly binds the latter. However, in structure (3)
the direct object the boys c-commands the indirect object each other and hence wrongly predicts the
(ii) is grammatical.
Multitasking, once believed to be a sign of productivity, is turning out to be not very desirable. It can
lead to accidents, negatively impacts ability to get focused and solve complex problems, and make
learning  less  efficient.  Therefore,  we  should  not  naively  adhere  to  our  old  assumption  about
multitasking.
In class A the teacher mainly assumes a supporter or facilitator role. This is evidenced by the facts
that the teacher motivates the students by providing a personal anecdote, lets the students do most of
the talking, monitors the class and offers feedback if needed. On the other hand, in class B the teacher
chiefly adopts the role of an instructor or controller. This is evidenced by the facts that the teacher
presents the rules to the students, leads choral work, does a lot of talking and shows intolerance toward
students' mistakes.
    As a result of these differences in teacher roles the two teachers show remarkably different aspects
in the classroom management. In terms of modes of classroom organization the teacher in Class A
chooses interaction-friendly grouping and seating while the teacher in Class B adopts non-interaction-
friendly grouping and seating. Concerning the contribution to the teaching and learning process the
teacher in Class A orients toward student-centered approaches whereas the teacher in Class B slants
toward teacher-centered approaches. As regards types of teaching and learning activities the teacher
in Class A favors communicative activities while the teacher in Class B prefers to mechanical drills.

There arose several complications in the medical experiment.
First, the same word for both blanks is “sound.” Second, the main idea of the passage is that the serial
processing  operations  based  on  the  phonics  approach  are  not  correct  since  some  sound  value  of
upcoming letters or words cannot be predicted until one knows the context containing the item.
The  appropriate  word  for  the  blank  is  imitation.  Second,  manufacturers  began  using  “distinctive”
names in order to give the impression that imitation foods were the  actual real items to consumers,
without breaking the Drug Act of 1906.
Mr. Song's class is based on the focus on forms approach, whereas Miss Oh uses the focus on form
approach. To be specific, Mr. Song explicitly provides grammatical explanation through meta-linguistic
terms. Miss Oh, on the other hand, helps students notice the target grammar within a reading text.
Mr.  Lee  wants  to  personalize  the  textbook  materials  to  meet  his  students'  needs  for  easier  writing
sections and their interests in sports. Accordingly, he, first, decides to add two pre-writing activities.
Moreover, he tries to reorder some reading texts according to students' interests
As  shown  in  the  data  given  in  (1)  and  (3),  schwa  deletion  occurs  in  fast  speech  when  a  schwa  is
preceded by a stressed vowel and followed by another schwa.
Mijin  uses  a  clarification  request  saying  "Could  you  repeat  what  you  said?"  or  "I  am  sorry?"  and
employs a comprehension check such as "You know what I mean?" In the case of Haerim, as she says
" Do you understand?" she uses a comprehension check only.
The  associative  use  in  accounts  for  the  use  of  the  definite  articles  in  the  sentence  .  The  speaker
assumes  that  the  listener  knows  that  a  taxi  must  have  a  driver  and  that  it  usually  has  passengers;
therefore, a definite article comes before both driver and passengers.
If the VP structure (4) in <A> fits (ii) in <B>, 'each other' occurs in the specifier position of VP and 'the
boys' appears in the complement position of the V'. In this case, according to the definition of the c-
command in <A>, the antecedent 'the boys' cannot c-command its anaphor 'each other'. This fact can
explain the ungrammaticlity of the sentence (ii) in <B>. On the other hand, if the VP structure (3) is
chosen, 'the boys' can c-command 'each other' and then the ungrammaticality of the sentence (ii) in
<B> cannot be explained.
Multitasking is an ineffective means of increasing one’s productivity. Multitasking, a term borrowed
from  computer  processing,  is  motivated  in  modern  life  by  the  desire  to  fulfill  many  demands
simultaneously. However, multitasking has been shown to cause many problems, such as increasing
risk in driving, reducing workplace productivity, and reducing the capacity for learning. Given this new
understanding, the practice of multitasking should not be encouraged.
In Class A the teacher carries out the roles of a facilitator and a resource person: first, she monitors
students' performances in groups and encourages them to actively participate in activities. Besides,
she supports them as needed. That is, she leads students to find their own pathways to success. On
the other hand, in Class B the teacher plays the role of a controller, whose job is to be always in charge
of every moment in the classroom. He determines what students do, when they should speak, and
what language forms they should use.
  Accordingly, the two teachers show several different aspects in the classroom management. In terms
of  learner  responsibility,  first  off,  the  teacher  in  Class  A  articulates  learning  objectives  to  facilitate
students'  active  learning  while  the  teacher  of  Class  B  directly  gives  grammatical  explanation  and
instruction without mentioning the learning objectives. Moreover, the classroom organization makes
differences between Class A and Class B. To encourage a learner-centered environment the teacher
of Class A divides the class into groups and allows students some choices in their groups. However,
The teacher of Class B works as a whole class in the teacher-fronted classroom by organizing drills
such as choral repetition.

Even though multitasking has been regarded as a useful strategy to increase productivity, there are
several disadvantages. First, using electronic devices such as cell phone during driving endangers
people. Second, multitasking actually decrease productivity in workplace as workers pay attention to
other tasks. Third, multitasking can negatively affect our way of learning in that it makes learning
fragmented and less flexible. Thus, assumption that it is better to do more things simultaneously should
be challenged.

The structure (4) can explain the ungrammaticality of (ii). When the sentnece follows the structure (4),
the antecedent 'the boys' cannot c-command its anaphor 'each other'. However, when we assume that
it  follows  the  structure  (3),  'the  boys'  can  c-command  'each  other'.  Thus,  the  structure  (3)  cannot
explain the ungrammaticality of (ii) like the structure (4).

unflexible and not organized. Thus, we should reconsider the idea of multitasking as a handy strategy
Firstly, the teachers in Class A and Class B show very different roles. The teacher in Class A plays the

The two sentences containing an unaccusative verb are sentence (3) and (5). This is because
"remain" and "arise" can undergo there inversion as follows: There remained several students in the
school library; There arose several complications in the medical experiment. The word "eat", "shop",
and "salute" do not allow there inversion as follows: *There ate several people in the Korean
restaurant; *There shopped several customers in the new shopping center; *There saluted several
soldiers in the military ceremony.
The appropriate word is "sound". Next, the main idea is as follows: Although the phonics approach
assumed that reading comprehension entails serial processing, this is not true because the sounds of
letters and words cannot be predicted without their surrounding context.
The word is "imitation". Manufactures started to use "distinctive names" to protect the bottom lines for
the cheap imitation. By using distinctive names, consumers were made to believe that they are buying
particular foods even though they were not. In this way, the imitators could sell imitation products
before the new law that was legislated in 1938.
Mr. Song's lesson is based on focus on formS. He aims to develop students' grammatical competence
by  explicitly  teaching  grammar  structures.  His  lessons  are  based  on  structural  syllabus  and  uses
metalinguistic  terms.  By  contrast,  Miss  Oh's  lesson  is  based  on  focus  on  form.  She  uses  input
enhancement  technique  by  italicizing  the  target  forms.  She  also  uses  meaning-focused  activity  by
checking the understanding of the reading text.
Mr. Lee wants to personalize the materials because he wants to suit his students' needs and
interests. First, he uses adding as material adaptation technique. He adds more pre-writing activities
to ease the difficulty of idea development. Second, he uses reordering by switching the two texts.
This will suit students' interest in sports.
The first condition for schwa deletion is as follows: Schwa deletion occurs when schwa is preceded
by a stressed syllable. The second condition is as follows: Schwa deletion occurs when schwa is
followed by an unstressed syllable.
First, Mijin uses clarification request by saying "Could you repeat what you said?" and "I am sorry?"

Associative use best accounts for the use of the two definite articles used in front of "driver" and
"passengers". This is because the speaker can assume that the listeners know "taxi" is related to
"passengers" and "driver". As "taxi" is mentioned in the first sentence, "driver" and "passengers" can
be used with definite articles in front of them.
The VP structure in (4) can account for the ungrammaticality of sentence (2) in <B>. This is because
the VP structure in (3) does not show that "the boys" and "each other" are c-commanded in sentence
(1),  but  not  in  sentence  (2).  However,  the  VP  structure  in  (4)  states  that  "each  other"  is  not  c-
commanded by "the boys" in sentence (2).
Recently,  multitasking  has  been  found  to  have  many  disadvantages  by  numerous  studies.  First,
multitasking  is  dangerous  when  one  is  driving  and  using  cell  phones.  Second,  multitasking  also
decreases  productivity  in  workplaces.  It  impairs  one's  ability  to  solve  complex  problem.  Third,
multitasking  is  harmful  to  our  learning.  It  harms  our  retention  of  learned  materials.  Therefore,  it  is
important to note that multitasking is not that beneficial as we think.

To begin with, the roles that the teachers take in class A and class B are different. First, the teacher
takes the roles as facilitator and resource in class A. More specifically, the teacher takes the role as a
resource in step 3 by providing help only when the students need the teacher. Also, the teacher takes
the roles as a facilitator in step 4 by encouraging reluctant students to participate in group activities.
Second, the teacher takes the role as instructor in class B. More specifically, the teacher instructs
students to chorally  repeat the sentences from the recording. Also, he explicitly corrects students'
errors.

In addition, the way the teacher manages the classroom is also very different in class A and class B.
First,  in  class  A,  the  teacher  takes  communicative  context  mode.  That  is,  the  teacher  encourages
meaning-focused  activities  like  a  consensus  building  activity.  Also,  the  teacher  gives  rather
unobtrustive feedback like repetition. Second, in class B, the teacher takes managerial mode. This is
because the teacher strictly manages the classroom activities. The teacher is utilizing the drills and
explicit feedback to control the students' activities.

It is predictive validity. The College Entrance Exam(CEE) scores can be said to predict the college

The sentences (iii) and (v) contain unaccusative verbs, "remain" and "arise." In these sentences, the
subjects originate in the complement position within the immediate V-bar projection of the verb, taking
a Theme role. Therefore, both pass the there insertion test as follows: (iii) "there remained several
students in the school library" and (v) "there arose several complications in the medical experiment."
The appropriate word for the blank is "sound." The phonics approach, which presupposes the serial
processing in reading, is contradicted by F. Smith in that the sound value of each letter in a word can
be assigned after the lexical or sentential context around the letter is determined.
The appropriate word for the blank is "imitation." Manufacturers of cheap imitation food started to
use "distinctive names" so that they could make the consumers believe that the products contain
the ingredients which have similar names to that of the products. In this way, they could sell the
imitation products without being illegal.

are able to focus on the target form as their primary focus is on meaning.

Mijin used clarification requests and comprehension checks. In her utterances, "could you repeat what

Associative use of the definite article explains the sentence in <B>. People are likely to asscociate the
word "taxi" with the word "driver" or "passenger," so the speaker of the sentence <B> assumes that
the listener knows the relationship between them. As a result, the speaker uses the definite article for
"driver" and "passenger" after the word "a taxi."
6. VP structure (4) can explain the ungrammaticality of sentence (ii) in <B>. If we apply the structure
(3) to the sentence (ii), the sentence becomes grammatical in that "the boys" in (ii) can c-command its
sister "each other." On the other hand, the (ii) is ungrammatical in (4) structure because the anaphor
"each other" in the higher NP cannot be c-commaded by its antecednet "the boys" in the lower NP.
VP structure (4) can explain the ungrammaticality of sentence (ii) in <B>. If we apply the structure (3)
to the sentence (ii), the sentence becomes grammatical in that "the boys" in (ii) can c-command its
sister "each other." On the other hand, the (ii) is ungrammatical in (4) structure because the anaphor

The idea that human multitasking, doing many things at once, has many advantages is contradicted
by modern research for three reasons. First, multitasking in driving and using electronic devices is
very  dangerous,  so  some  countries  made  this  multitasking  illegal.  Second,  multitasking  is
counterproductive  in  working  places  because  it  prevents  people  from  being  involved  in  complex
problems.  Lastly,  multitasking  distracted  from  learning  process.  Learning  from  multitasking  is  not
flexible  and  fragmented,  so  the  retrievement  from  memory  becomes  difficult.  For  these  reasons,  it
seems that it is time to change the idea that doing more is better.

(1st paragraph) The teacher in class A plays a role as a facilitater(오타감점있을듯  facilitator입니다)
or helper, whereas the teacher in class B is a person who conveys knowledge. In class A, the teacher
facilitates  learning  by  activating  schemata  in  the  beginning,  employing  cooperative  learning,  and
encouraging students to participate in the activity. In this student-centered class, the teacher and the
students  are  the  equal  participants  of  the  class.  However,  in  class  B,  the  teacher  conveys  the
knowledge of the target form in an one-directed way. The students just listen and repeat in this teacher-
centered class.
(2nd paragraph) The teacher in class A manages the class in a communicative way. He or she uses
students' opinions in activity and uses repetition as a feedback so that the students can correct the
errors by themselves, making them autonomous learners. On the other hand, the teacher in class B
uses mechanical drills and does not reflect students' opinions in class. He or she also uses explicit
correction as a feedback and does not give students the chance to correct errors by themselves.

Schwa can be deleted in fast speech under the following two phonetic conditions. First, it has to be
preceded by a stressed syllable. Second, it has to be followed by another schwa.

The associative use in <A> best accounts for the use of the definite articles in <B>. As the speaker
assumes that the listener knows that a taxi must have a driver and it normally has passengers, a definite
article 'the' comes before both 'driver' and 'passengers'.
(4)  can  account  for  the  ungrammaticality  of  sentence  (ii).  If  we  apply  (3)  as  a  structure  of  (ii),  the
anaphor each other' satisfies all the conditions to be bound, since it is coindexed with 'the boys' and
is c-commanded by its sister 'the boys'. So, it can't explain the ungrammaticality of (ii). In contrast, if
we apply (4) structure, 'each other' cannot be c-commanded by the boys. Therefore, only (4) structure
can account for the ungrammaticality of (ii).
The  assumption  that  multitasking  is  an  efficient  strategy  for  improving  productivity  is  now  being
challenged. Recently,  it  is  found  that  multitasking  while  driving,  such  as  using  cell  phones,  can  be
fatally  dangerous.  Also,  multitasking  decreases  productivity  in  the  workplace  as  well  as  has  bad
influence on learning by making it fragmented and less flexible. Therefore, we should no longer try to
do many things at the same time.
In  Class  A,  the  teacher  takes  the  roles  of  a  facilitator  and  a  helper.  The  teacher  walks  around  the
classroom  and  keeps  encouraging  students  to  participate  in  the  discussion,  facilitating  students'
learning process. Also, the teacher monitors students' summarizing and provides help as needed. On
the other hand, in Class B, the teacher carries the roles of a controller and a director. The teacher
instructs students to pay attention to the class, controlling them strictly, and directs every activity that
students must do. Class A and Class B differ a lot in how the teacher manages the classroom. In terms
of physical environment, the teacher in Class A divides students into groups to make learner-centered
and interactive class. In contrast, the teacher in Class B stays in front of the board for the whole class,
which makes a highly teacher-centered class. Moreover, Class A and Class B are contrastive in class
atmosphere, which is revealed through the different extent to which learner autonomy is fostered. In
Class A, the teacher tries to give autonomy and responsibility to students, by letting them choose what
they want in their groups. On the other hand, the teacher in Class B doesn't let students make any
choice in the class, which leads to students' lower responsibility for the class.

Among the senior teacher's suggestions, Ms. Shin's class conform to 'Objective' and 'Strategy'. First,
her  class  followed  the  objective  by  focusing  on  language  functions.  She  set  a  function  of  'making
requests' as  her  class  objective  and  encouraged students  to  use  the  question  forms  and  ask  their
partner for the necessary information to fill in the book order form. Second, she asked students to use
the communication strategy. When students didn't come up with the exact words to express meaning,
they were encouraged to use 'approximation' and 'nonverbal signal' strategy by using similar words
they knew or even gestures.
On the other hand, there are two suggestions Ms. Shin's class did not conform to: 'Error targeted',
and 'Feedback'. As for treating errors, she focused not on global errors but on local errors. She gave
students  feedback  on  their  errors  of  missing  's'  in  some  verbs  but  this  error  does  not  impede
communication  of  meaning.  Next,  as  for  feedback,  she  provided  correction  explicitly.  Rather  than
providing feedback implicitly during the activity, Ms. Shin provided explicit feedback after the activity
by  overtly  informing  students  that  they  made  errors  of  missing  's'  and  provided  the  correct  form
explicitly.

students apply the rule into writing through some practices. Inductive learning is applied for Class B.

First, Ms. Song used mechanical and meaningful drills to let her students practice the target structure
of future tense. She first provides the cue phrases with the pictures and students are allowed to repeat
the same structures, substituting with the given phrases. After that, they make their phrases based on
the  pictures  to  substitute  in  the  target  structure.  Teacher's  response  is  just  to  evaluate  whether
student's answers are correct or not, rather than commenting on meaning.
There are two changes after the consultation. First Ms. Song used different question types. Before,
she used display questions to ask for the predetermined correct answers. Later, she used referential
questions, where students answer their own ideas in real-life to facilitate communicative competence.
For another change, Ms. Song used different feedback on the students' answers. After consultation,
she gave some feedback on meaning to expand students' communicative competence compared to
the feedback on form in pre-consultation. (153 words)

The event that the sentence (a) of (i) describes is telic, whereas the event that the sentence (b) of (i)
describes is atelic. The sentence (b) of (ii) ambiguous because in adverbial in it can have either the
event duration interpretation or the event delay interpretation. That is, the sentence (b) of (ii) can be
interpreted in two different ways. One is that it will take five minutes for John to finish eating the pizza.
The other is that John will eat the pizza five minutes from now.

The teacher's two corrective feedback utterances are the followings: "You didn't study yesterday?" and
"Well, Minjae, “don't had" is not the right past tense form. The former utterance is an example of recast
and the latter one is an example of metalinguistic feedback. The use of recast satisfies the teacher's
beliefs as the choice of effective corrective feedback because it treats the learner's error implicitly so
that it does not embarrass the learner inadvertently and disrupt the flow of ongoing communication, It
also contains a targetlike alternative form to the learner's ill-formed output, which enables the learner
to make a comparison of his or her problematic form and its correct form.
The two well-applied principles are reliability and authenticity. The test is dependable because there
were no errors in scoring and also authentic because the topics were relevant to the student's real life,
The two poorly-applied principles are validity and washback. The test is not valid because the tasks
were unfamiliar and were never dealt in class. It does not have washback because the teacher didn't
go over the test to give feedback or comments on what the student should focus on in the future.

The underlined PP in (a) in <B>, with a knee injury is an Adjunct, whereas the underlined PP in (b) in
<B>, for the PGA title is a Complement. One evidence to support this identification comes from the
following pair of ungrammatical and grammatical NPs: *A contender with a knee injury for the PGA
title, A contender for the PGA title with a knee injury. The other evidence comes from the following
ungrammatical and grammatical wh-questions: *What injury is he a contender with? , What title is he
a contender for?

Before  the  consultation,  the  teacher  utilized  the  pattern  drill  to  teach  the  target  structure,  For

feedback he used in the class. Before the consultation, he only uses the display questions, which
elicit the answers that are already known. After the consultation, he switches the question types to
referential questions which require the answers that are unknown. In terms of the type of feedback,
he used the explicit feedback by saying "No, you should say "Tom will visit a museum". Afte the
consultation, however, his use of explicit feedback used the implicit feedback by saying "I take guitar

The event described by (ia) is telic; the situation portrayed by (ib) is atelic. The sentence (iib) is
ambiguous since the in adverbial in it results in two readings[interpretations]:  ①  It will take five

minutes for John to eat the pizza. (event duration)  ②  John will eat the pizza after five minutes [five
minutes from now]. (event delay)

Group1: riddle, saddle. Battle
Group2: monitor, humanity, comedy
The rule for froup1 is that alveolar stops become a flap when they are  located between a stressed
vowel and a syllabic lateral [a syllabic /l/]. The alveolar stops in Group2 becomes a flap when they
occur between two unstressed vowels.

The predicate in (ia) describes a telic event, whereas the one in (ib) describes an atelic event. The
sentence in (iib) is ambiguous because the in adverbial allows for both an event delay interpretation
(i.e., John will commence the act of eating in five minutes) and an event duration interpretation (i.e.,

“You didn’t study yesterday?” is a recast by the teacher, and “Well, Minjae, ‘don’t had’ is not the right
past tense form,” is the teacher’s explicit metalinguistic feedback. The recast reflects Mr. Jeon’s beliefs
because it does not explicitly indicate that an error has occurred and because it contains a targetlike
alternative to the learner’s ill-formed output.

13  One of the two well-applied principles is reliability, which is evident in the statement that there were
no errors in scoring. The other is authenticity because the topics were very relevant to the student’s
real  life.  One  poorly-applied  principle  is  validity  because  the  achievement  test  included  tasks  not
covered in class. Washback is another poorly-applied principle in that after the test the student feels
not sure how to improve reading skills and get prepared for similar future tests.
the unusual / The author does not think that it is likely that someone would refuse a large inheritance

One strong point is the fact that the teacher conducted a needs analysis using a survey and interviews
and incorporated the results of the analysis in her materials, contents, and activities, thus catering to
her  students’  needs.  One  weak  point  of  the  teacher’s  course  is  that  speaking  was  not  assessed
regularly  enough  to  allow  the  teacher  to  monitor  her  students’  progress  in  speaking  ability.  One
possible  way  to  address  the  weakness  is  by  having  informal  assessment  of  speaking  such  as
observations, self- and peer-assessment at regular intervals.
The words riddle, saddle, battle, monitor, humanity, and comedy cannot be accounted for by the
underlined rule. A flapping rule for the first three words is that alveolar stops become a flap when they
are located between a stressed vowel and a syllabic /l/. For the last three words, we need a flapping
rule to the effect that alveolar stops become a flap between two unstressed vowels, the first of which
is preceded by a stressed syllable.

Teacher A applied deductive learning in that students were given the rule first and then asked to apply
the  rule  in  the  writing  exercises.  Teacher  B,  on  the  other  hand,  applied  inductive  learning  in  that
students were asked to examine examples first and then work out the rule that could account for the
examples.
The underlined PP in B(a) performs the grammatical function of an adjunct, as (i) and (ii) show, while
that in B(b) performs the grammatical function of a complement, as (iii) and (v) illustrate.
  (i) *A contender with a knee injury for the PGA title

Korea’s involvement in the global community continues to expand. Goods produced in Korea are
extremely popular. In addition, Korean culture has generated a lot of interest in neighboring countries.
This happened due partly to luck but mostly to smart strategy by Koreans. Therefore, in order to further

Before the consultation, Ms. Song used a picture-cued substitution drill in teaching grammatical
structures.  She  provided  the  picture  cues  and  the  expressions  necessary  for  participating  in  the
activity, and thus all that students had to do was to substitute the subjects and the verb phrases which
are supplied in the pictures and the teacher’s verbal prompts. In short, the technique Ms. Song used
was very mechanical because students engaged in simple substitution.
  After the consultation, however, Ms. Song introduced two changes into her class. First, she changed
the way she offered feedback on students’ erroneous output. Before the consultation, she provided
explicit teacher correction, but after the consultation she offered clarification requests in the form of
repetitions which served as prompts for students’ self-correction. Second, Ms. Song changed the way
she  asked  questions.  She  used  display  questions  before  the  consultation,  while  she  employed
referential  questions  that  encouraged  students  to  express  personal  meanings  using  the  linguistic
resources at their disposal.

In <B>, (ia) is telic, while (ib) is atelic. The sentence in (iib) is ambiguous and has two readings. The
first  reading  is  a  (telic)  event  of  duration  interpretation,  ‘John  will  finish  eating  the  pizza  within  five
minutes.’ and the second reading is an (atelic) event of delay interpretation: 'John will eat the pizza
after five minutes.'

12  As corrective feedback on a student’s error, the teacher used a recast type feedback of “you didn’t
study yesterday” and the metalinguistic feedback “didn’t had is not the right past tense form” in the
classroom  conversation.  However,  Mr.  Joen  thinks  that  the  recast  type  feedback  is  more  effective
because it does not explicitly indicate the error but maintains the communicative flow with the target-
like form.

All the words that do not belong to the underlined rule in <A> are ‘riddle’, ‘saddle’, battle’, ‘monitor’,
‘humanity’, and ‘comedy’. These words are divided into two groups: ‘riddle, saddle, battle’ and ‘monitor,
humanity, comedy’. The rule for the first group is that alveolar stops /t/ and /d/ are flapped when they
occur between a stressed vowel and (syllabic) liquid /l/, and the rule for the second group is that the
flapping occurs between two unstressed vowels.

The type of learning that occurs in Teacher A’s class is deductive learning since the teacher explains
the rule of the if -clause and then gives students exercises in which they apply the rule. On the other
hand, Teacher B’s class orients students toward inductive learning because he presents the examples
of the if-clause, and then students have to infer the rule by themselves.
In <B>, the PP in (a) is an Adjunct, while the PP in (b) is a Complement. As for a pair of NPs, the NP
with a Complement + an Adjunct in (ia) is grammatical but the NP with an Adjunct + a Complement in
(ib) is ungrammatical.
      (i) a. a contender for the PGA title with a knee injury
            b. *a contender with a knee injury for the PGA title
As  for  a  pair  of  wh-questions,  the  wh-phrase  within  the  PP  Adjunct  in  (iia)  cannot  be  preposed;  in
contrast, the wh-phrase within the PP Complement in (iib) can.
    (ii) a. *What part (kind) of injury is he a contender with?

Korea  has  been  continuously  increasing  its  participation  in  the  global  community,  both  in  terms  of
culture  and  business,  through  good  fortune  and  planning.  The  interest  in  Korean  products  from
overseas  has  seen  a  huge  increase,  especially  regarding  electronics  and  automotive  industries.
Likewise,  the  Korean  cultural  contents  such  as  television  programming,  music,  and  cuisine,  has
become fashionable outside of Korea and inspired further export. Thus, Korea can continue to flourish
if it controls its place and growth on the global stage.
Ms. Song used a pattern- drill practice activity before the consultation. Particularly, she provided a
cued-substitution drill which is a kind of controlled practice activity where students substitute taking
cues from the teacher even without knowing the meaning of the target grammatical item (i.e., future
tense).
However, after receiving advice from Mr. Cho, Ms. Song made two major changes in class. Firstly, in
terms of questions types, she changed display questions into referential questions so that students
were able to personalize the future tense. That is to say, before consultation, the students mechanically
practiced the future tense with the given information, but after the consultation, students used it to talk
about their future plans based on the real information. Secondly, concerning the type of feedback on
students’ errors, before the consultation, she used explicit correction, but after the consultation, she
used repetition whose type leaded students to correct the errors by themselves.(self-correct).

10  Sentence (ia) describes a telic event, [in that the prepositional phrase(PP) to the park as a goal implies
a natural end point]. Meanwhile, sentence (ib) depicts an atelic event [because the PP in the park as a
location cannot provide any information about when the activity of walking ends]. The ambiguity occurs
in sentence (iib) because the predicate “eat the pizza” describes a telic event with a natural end point.
It can be interpreted as the event duration and the event delay as in (1) and (2), respectively.
Plants/  If  global  temperature  increases  by  more  than  2  degrees  Celsius,  the  permafrost  decays,
releases carbons into the atmosphere, and finally dries out. Thus, the outgassing effect will become
worse due to the rise of carbon concentrations in the air.
In <B>, the teacher uses two types of corrective feedbacks: recast in the utterance “You didn’t study
yesterday?” and metalinguistic feedback in “Well, Minjae, “don’t had” is not the right past tense form.”
Based on <A>, Mr. Jeon believes that the utterance “You didn’t study yesterday?” is effective feedback
as an implicit way of correction because it provides a target-like alternative without interrupting the
flow of communication.
The two well-applied principles of language assessment are reliability and authenticity, whereas the
two  poorly-applied  principles  are  validity-especially,  content  validity-and  washback.  Based  on  the
student’s post-exam reflection, the scoring process of the test was reliable and the test dealt with the
relevant topics to real-life. However, validity is poorly applied in the test because it covers the tasks
which  are  unfamiliar  and  were  not  even  dealt  with  in  the  classroom.  In  addition,  the  test  lacks
washback, in that no feedback or comments were not given to the students after the assessment.

The words in <B> — riddle, monitor, saddle, humanity, battle, and comedy    cannot be accounted for
by the underlined rule given in Depending on the contexts where flapping occurs, they are categorized
into two groups as follows:
Group l : riddle, saddle, battle
Group 2: monitor, humanity, comedy
The alveolar stops /t, d/ in Group I become a flapped sound between a stressed vowel and a syllabic
lateral, whereas /t, d/ in Group 2 become a flap when they occurs between two unstressed vowels,
and the first unstressed vowels are preceded by nasals. Although the first vowel is stressed in this
case, this is not a necessary condition for applying the rule.

the target form and asks students to practice it with the given examples. Teacher B, on the other hand,
uses inductive learning by asking students to analyze the examples by reformulating incorrect forms

Teacher A’s class is based on deductive learning in that he explicitly taught the target rule firstly, and
the students are required to apply the rule to the data as transformation drill and writing. Teacher B’s
class  is  based  on  inductive  learning  because  he  provided  students  with  data  as  correct  forms  in
reformulation text and asks students to compare/contrast between incorrect forms and correct forms.

1. drill유형:    pattern drill in the form of cue-response drill
Ss practice target structure “future tense”
• Verbal cue with picture “ride a bike” and response” John will ride a bike.”
• Nonverbal cue as picture with question “what will they do?” – response “ they will go to a movie”
(본인이  생각하기에  더  썼으면  좋았을  내용  /  그러나  당시엔  기억  안  나서  못씀

: picture -> context제공하므로  meaningful  하다라는  점.  추가되면  좋을  듯!!    )
2. Type of question and feedback changed
Question: display question -> referential question
1) display: predetermined answer, elicit answer, check-up student’s knowledge and comprehension
2) referential: no predetermined answer, T learns new info from Ss, info gap -> active interaction b/w
T & Ss (authentic, real-like라는  말을  썼는지  안썼는지  기억  안남)
  Feedback: explicit correction -> repetition (implicit)
1) Explicit correction: indicate that error occurs, correct form을  줌으로써  self- correct기회를  안  줌.

2) repetition: T repeat the Ss’ erroneous utterance, correct input안줌으로써  self-correct  기회를  줌.

First, (ia) describes a telic event, while (ib) describes an atelic event. Second, (iib) is ambiguous
because it has both of the ‘event duration’ and ‘event delay’ readings. In the first reading, (iib) means
John will finish eating the pizza within five minutes, In the second reading, (iib) means John will start
eating pizza after five minutes from now.

“You didn’t study yesterday?” and “Well, Minjae, “don’t had” is not the right past tense form.” are the
corrective  feedback  utterances  in  <B>.  The  former  is  ‘recast’,  while  the  latter  is  ‘metalinguistic
feedback’. Only the recast of the teacher in <B> meets Mr. Jeon’s belief since it implicitly indicates the
error  and  gives  an  alternative  well-formed  utterance  to  the  student.  On  the  other  hand,  the  latter,
metalinguistic feedback, explicitly corrects the error and dose not give any alternative correct form to
the student.

First, ‘riddle, saddle, battle, monitor, humanity, comedy’ cannot be accounted for by the underlined
rule  in  <A>.  The  rule  for  the  first  three  words  are  as  follows:  Alveolar  stops  become  a  flap  when
preceded by a stressed vowel and followed by syllabic ‘I’. The rule for  the last three words are as
follows: Alveolar stops become a flap between two unstressed vowels.

the students to write a well-organized suggestion letter by demonstrating how to use the discourse
markers to connect sentences coherently. To be specific, the students learn how to use the markers
like ‘firstly’ or ‘as a result’ to produce an organized letter.
abused statistic / The average Yaleman’s annual income could be misleading because it is not certain

is likely that the average cannot represent the overall tendency.
Deductive learning is applied to Teacher A's class, whereas inductive learning is applied to Teacher
B's class. In the class of Teacher A, explicit explanations on the target past tense verb are given to the
students first. Then, the students are asked to apply the rule to the specific instances. In contrast, the
students in Teacher B's class are given the specific incidents first and then are required to discover
the rule from the data.
First,  the  underlined  PPs  in  'a'  and  'b'  are  and  an  Adjunct  and  a  Complement,  respectively.  The
evidence for this are as follows:

Today, in the globalized world, Korea is expanding its role both in terms of economy and culture. That
is, its electronic and automotive products as well as cultural products are getting popular among the
global community. In fact, this success is not a coincidence, given that Korea has been planning for
globalization for a long time, waiting for the right place and time. To maintain the momentum of its

The technique Ms. Song used before consultation is a substitution drill. She suggests the sentence
"She will go swimming." first, and then shows a picture of 'John riding a bike' and suggests a  verb
phrase 'ride a bike'. Then, students are asked to make a sentence using provided verb phrase, which
is a simple substitution of the verb phrase replacing ‘go swimming' with 'ride a bike'.
After the consultation, she made two changes. First, she changed the types of questions. Before the
consultation, she asked display questions such as "What will they do?", which allows only a limited set
of answers. However, after the consultation, she used referential questions like "what will you do this
vacation?", which is a real asking of the students' personal plans. Second, the teacher changed the
types of feedback. Before Mr. Cho's advice, she gave explicit corrections such as 'No, you should say,
"Tom will visit a museum", which directly gives the alternative correct form. After the advice, she used
repetition as a corrective feedback in the utterance "I go to Grandma's house?", which simply repeats
the ill-formed output to indicate the error. It pushes the student to self-correct their errors.

In (i), the first sentence is telic and the second is atelic, In (ii), sentence 'b' is ambiguous as both event
delay and event duration interpretations are possible. With the event delay interpretation, 'b' means "At
the  end  of  five  minutes  from  now,  John  will  start  to  eat  the  pizza",  but  with  an  event  duration
interpretation, it means "John will finish eating the pizza in five minutes"
Two  corrective  feedback  utterance  are  “You  didn’t  study  yesterday?,”  which  is  recast,  and  “Well,
Minjae, ‘don’t had’ is not the right past tense form,” which is metalinguistic feedback. Teacher’s first
feedback (recast) did not indicate that  the student committed an error so it maintained  the flow of
ongoing communication. At the same time, the teacher implicitly suggested a targetlike alternative to
the student’s erroneous output-‘didn’t study’ instead of ‘don’t studied.’
One strong point is that the teacher conducted needs analysis about what students want to learn, and
then reflected it in designing her lesson objectives, contents, and activities. One weak point is that the
teacher did not assess students' developmental process in the middle of the course. As a solution, the
teacher  can  conduct  formative  assessment  regularly,  focusing  on  students'  ongoing  and  further
development.
Schema/  To  enable  the  students  to  write  a  well-organized  suggestion  letter,  the  teacher  taught
cohesive markers like 'Firstly, So, and Therefore' in the end of the Stage 2. As using these markers
directly contributes to the organization of the letter, students can connect the sentences coherently
and make their letters more cohesive.
PP 'with a knee injury' is an adjunct and PP 'for the PGA title' is a complement. As for a pair of NPS, "a
contender for the PGA title with a knee injury" is grammatical while *a contender with a knee injury for
the PGA title" is ungrammatical. In relation to Wh-movement, "What title is he a contender for?" is
grammatical while "*Which injury is he a contender with?" is ungrammatical.
Ms. Song employed a 'substitution drill technique before the consultation. She gives a sentence "She
will go swimming" first, and offers a picture cue with a phrase. Then, the students in turn are asked to
make a new sentence by putting the cue into the proper place in the given sentence like "John will

ride a bike" and "Mary will play the piano",
Two  changes  that  Ms.  Song  made  are  as  follows,  First,  she  used  other  types  of  questions.  Before
consultation, the teacher provided display questions like "What will they do?", which have a very limited
set of answers only. After consultation, on the other hand, the teacher. gave referential questions like
"Do you have any plans?", encouraging students to answer based on their own personal experience,
Second,  she  provided  other  types  of  feedback.  Before  consultation,  the  teacher  gave  explicit
corrections like "You should say, 'Tom will visit a museum", suggesting the correct form directly. After
the consultation, however, she gave students opportunities to self-correct by using the repetition like
"I go to Grandma's house?"

In this conversation, the uptake takes place in the student's fourth utterance, "put chickens in oil, very
hot oil, kind of bake them.” Here, s/he uses circumlocution as a communication strategy, which is to
describe or exemplify the target object of the action for the verb "fry(fried).”

In the underlined words, the narrator suggests the uncertainty and lack of direction of a human being
in front of greater forces like mortality and the process of history. For example, first, the protagonist is
wandering(walking through) “the streets” aimlessly just as a lifeless fallen leaf is blown in the streets
without  a  definite  end.  Second,  hearing  the  ghostly “voices,” he  realizes “the  limitation  of
life” as “unsure” as a blown leaf’s future.
The  sources  of  the  ambiguity  in  (B)  are  differing  structures  and  homonymy.  In  the  structure
ambiguity, “John’s nose ring” can be a noun object of the main verb “saw” and the one reading is ‘Mary
saw the nose ring which John wore.’ and the other reading is ‘Mary saw John, and 'John's nose was
ringing.’ because ‘John’s  nose’ and ‘ring’ can  be  divided  into  a  noun  and  a  verb.  In  terms  of
homonymy, ‘ring’ as a noun can be interpreted as a piece of jewelry and as a verb, ‘to ring.
Tool C is recommendable for Ms. Park with the following two reasons. First, as a real-time interaction
tool,  it enables  students to  get  ready  for  offline  discussion.  Second,  since  it  can  save  and  archive
students' online production(transcripts of online interaction) the teacher can easily provide feedback
and correction on students' errors.
 First, the underlined words mean that “junk DNA” makes administrative decisions to have other DNA
either work or not, just like a middle manager of a factory. This realization expands the possibility to
cure diseases caused by genetic mutation because now it is possible for researchers not to examine
the bad gene itself but to intervene those “supervisors,” or the middle managers which decide the
behavior of the bad gene. Its number is a lot more than that of the gene; thus, the possibility of cure is
far more increased as well.
In American English of (1b) and (2b), /j/ cannot follow alveolar consonants when they are obstruent
sounds  /t,  d  s,  z/,  regardless  of  stress  placement.  In  (1b)  and  (3),  when  alveolar  consonants  are
sonorant sounds /n, l/, /j/ also cannot follow them if it is in stressed syllable but /j/ can follow them if it
is in unstressed syllable.
The underlined adverb, ‘rarely’ in (i) belongs to a usually type and the adverb ‘slowly’ in (ii) belongs to
a carefully type. ‘rarely’ can represent the two paraphrases as follows: it is rare that John talks with
philosophers, and it is rarely the case that John talks with philosophers. However, ‘slowly’ cannot be
paraphrased like the followings: *It is slow that the fish swims, and *It is slowly the case that the fish
swims.
Disposable  products  and  durable  goods  are  both  beneficial  to  the  economy.  To  begin  with,  since
people use disposable goods for a very short time or even only once, manufacturing them promotes

김재균

(채점

포인트)

2

innovation of designs and large employment of the industry. Consequently, it is conducive to economic
growth. Durable products also serve long-standing economic substantiality because they require the
development of the secondary industry providing the supply of parts and repairs necessary for long-
term use of products.
   On  the  other  hand,  disposable  products  and  durable  products  have  different  impact  on  the
environment. First, disposable products harm environment because they generate much waste some
of which is hard to decompose. In contrast, durable products help preservation of environment. They
reduce  pollution,  residual  waste  and  landfill  to  bury  the  waste.  In  short,  durable  goods  are
environmental friendly while disposable products damage environment.
According  to  the  students’ comments,  the  teacher's  lesson  shows  one  strong  point  and  one
problem: the use of authentic material and the teacher’s inappropriate correction method. One feature
of the teacher's lesson that students like is  the use of authentic materials, which motivate students
and makes them deeply involved in the lesson. Also, they enable students to clearly understand the
words and expressions related to the day's topic as well.
    However, they do not like the teacher's direct correction, which deprives them of the responsibility
in  learning  and  raises  their  affective  filter.  Thus,  as  alternative  ways,  self-correction  and  peer-
correction could be suggested. For instance, self-correction such as elicitation and repetition  could
give  students  an  opportunity to  reflect(locate) their  errors  and  reformulate  them.  Plus,  as  for  peer
correction,  it  is  more  comfortable  for  students  to exchange feedbacks  on  their  errors instead  of
getting teacher’s direct correction(feedback).

출제자가  원래  의도한  답은  둘째  단락  밑에서  4번째  줄에서  다소  강조되는  문맥에서  나오는

pedigree로  보여지나,  의미상으로  보면  talent  가능한  것으로  사료됨.

structural(syntactic),  lexical  주어진  자료  (A),  (B)  가  원작문에  비교해서  어떤  부분을  주로

고쳤는지  알  수  있는  문제.  다만  답안을  기입할  때  둘  다  형용사로  쓰는  게  완벽함

discriminality(or  constituency),  distractors  해당  문항이  상위권과  하위권의  차별성을  보여주지

못할  때  변별도가  부족하게  됨.  두번째  빈칸은  선택지가  매력적인  오답으로  기능하지  못하는

경우와  그  반대로  비정상적으로  많은  선택을  받을  경우의  문제임.  다만  기입할  때  선택지  B,  C

에  대한  문제이므로,  복수형으로  기입해야  정확함.

transactional  주어진  대화가  사실적  정보에  근거한  말하기를  통해  이루어지고  있음이  핵심.

쓰여서  답이  충분히  rest  도  될  수  있지만, ‘come to-‘에서  to-를  전치사  로  간주하고  뒤에  명사를

쓰는  일도  충분히  맞는  문장이  됨.  따라서, equanimity도  아무  문제  없는  답이라고  해야  맞음

allophone,  onset  /t/의  상보적  분포를  다루면서  그에  관한  여러  이음  (allophones)들을  소개

First, students will be able to transform the verb-oriented expressions into noun-oriented ones when
they intended to convey basically identical message. For example, students can transform “He works
hard” into “He is a hard worker”. Second, students will be able to identify in English use. For instance,
they can avoid using the ungrammatical sentences such as “My nose is sick”.

#  동사  중심의  표현과  명사  중심의  표현의  차이를  식별할  수  있다.

#  정문이  되는  동사  중심의  표현을  명사  중심의  표현으로  바꿔  쓸  수  있다.

#  동사  중심의  표현과  관련하여  비문을  식별하고  명사  중심의  정문으로  바꿔  쓸  수  있다.
The  uptake  takes  place  when  the  student  utters,  “Uh, you  know,  put  chickens  ..bake  them”  In  this

2

utterance, he employs the strategy of circumlocution (that provide loosely paraphrased expressions
instead of the correct target form). In this case the students did not know the accurate target form ‘fry’,
so  he  produced  an  erroneous  form  ‘fly’.  After  being  pushed  to  modify  the  error,  he  attempted  to
continue communication by using the circumlocution expression.
(채점  기준)

The given sentence in <B> shows the case of ambiguity due to different structure and homonymy.
'John's nose ring can be analyzed into [NP John's nose ring] or [NP John's nose] [VP ring]. In these
cases. ring is a homonymous word: it means a type of ornament in [Np John's nose ring] or the action
of making snorting sounds in [VP ring].
(채점  기준)

  1 점: 유전자의  중간적  통제가  갖는  미래  치료에서  의미가  치료를  시도할  수  있는 목록을

  2 점: 특별히, 유전자의  중간적  통제는  변형된  유전자  자체를  제거하지는  않지만, 나쁜  유전자의

표출을  허용하는  유전자  조각  중  하나는  제거하는  것임을  서술했다.
Unlike  British  English  (BE),  American  English  (AE)  allows  the  glide  /j/  only  in  unstressed  syllable,
following an alveolar sonorant. In (1a/b), only BE allows /j/ under the environment of stressed syllables,
regardless of sonority. In (2a/b), only BE, not AE, alows /j/ when it follows an obstruent, regardless of
stress. In (3a/b) only, AE allows /j/ when it occurs following sonorants such as /n/ or /l/ in unstressed
syllables.
(채점  기준)

  2 점: 영국식  영어와  달리  미국식  영어에서 /j/는  그  분포가  제약되는데  비강세  음절에서  치경

저해음  다음에만  허용됨을  명시했다.

  1 점: 1a/b): 강세  음절에서  비교되면, 선행하는  치경음이  공명음이건  저해음이건  영국

영어에만 /j/가  나타남.

  1 점: 2a/b): 강세  음절에서건  비강세  음절에서건  간에, 치경  저해음에  속하는 /s/  ./z/ 다음에는

영국  영어는 /j/가  나타나는데  반해  미국  영어는  나타나지  않음.

  1 점: 3a/b): 비강세  음절이면서  공명음인  치경음이  선행하면  두  영어  모두 /j/가  나타남. 즉  이

조건에서만  미국  영어에서도 /j/가  허용됨.
The adverb ‘rarely’ is a ‘usually’ type (frequency adverb) while the adverb ‘slowly’ is a ‘carefully’ type
(manner adverb). We can say, for example, ‘It is rare that John comes..’ or ‘It is rarely the case that
John comes..’ We cannot say, however, ‘It is slow that John drives ..’ or ‘It is slowly the case that John
drives ..’
1 점: rarely 와 slowly 가  각각 usually 와 carefully 유형임을  식별했다. 2 점: Rarely 를 (2)a, b 의  식형에

대입한  적절한  예시를  서술했다. (a, b 각 1 점씩)2 점: Slowly 를 (3)b, c 와  동일한  형태의  비문으로

예시하며  설명했다. (b, c 각 1 점씩)

술

형

In economic dimension, disposable products help economic growth. They help create new designs

and employments, for instance. Also, in case of durable products, they contribute to long-term

benefits in economy though they cause short-term reduction in sale. Durable products can foster

secondary industries in relation to supplying parts and repairing.

As  for  environmental  issues,  on  the  other  hand,  disposable  products  have  only  negative

properties. They do not decompose in the nature while not contributing anything positive to it.

Durable products are so environment-friendly, however. They reduce the emission of pollutants

and require fewer landfills. These make durable products good choice in terms of environment.

(채점  기준)

 2 점: 경제적  측면에서 1 회용  제품은  경제  성장에  도움  됨을  서술했다. 그  예로서  새  디자인을

만들게  하고  고용을  창출함을  지적하며  뒷받침  했다.

2 점: 경제적  측면에서  오래  쓰는  제품은  비록  당장은  판매  감소를  유발해도, 장기적으로  이익이

됨을  서술했다. 그  예로써 2 차  산업  육성에  도움  됨을  지적하며  뒷받침  했다.

줄고  매립지가  덜  필요함을  지적하며  뒷받침  했다.

2

  Students liked the teacher’s lesson because it employed the topic related to real life, ‘cooking’. This
strong point contributes to motivating students and giving them interests in the learning  material. It
also makes students clearly understand the meanings of the target forms.
  The problem of the teacher’s lesson lies in that students cannot have enough opportunities for errorr
correction by themselves or with peers. This problem is suggested by Sumi and Inho at the ends of
their opinions. To address this weak point, students are suggested to correct errors individually and
in pairs, with enough time. Individually, students have time to reconsider their erroneous expressions
and attempt to find out the alternative forms, mainly depending on their own ability of inference. This

will give them the opportunity to tackle linguistic problems with their own responsibility. In pairs, each
student  observes  their  partner’s  expressions  and  writing  down  their  errors.  Then,  they  exchange
feedback  for  error  correction  with  each  other.  This  will  enable  students  to  overcome  linguistic
problems through cooperative process.
(채점  기준)

1 점: 학생들이  주어진  수업을  좋아하는  근거는  실제  생활에  관련된  소재로  된  학습임을

지적했다.

2 점: 위의  주장과  관련한  두  가지  이유로  첫째는  동기/흥미  유발에  유리한  점, 둘째는  대상

형태를  더  명쾌하게  이해시킬  수  있음을  서술했다. (본문의  근거  압축  인용  필요)

1 점: 이  수업의  문제점은  학생들이  충분한  기회를  갖고  스스로  오류  수정을  해볼  수  없다는  데

있음을  지적했다.

There are two lessen objectives in this lesson: 1. Students will be able to raise cultural awareness
about the noun-oriented expressions and verb-oriented expressions., and 2. Students will be able to

. 'Uh, you know~'에서  uptake가  일어났다.  또한, circulocution이  사용되었는데  이는  a strategy that

 Different structure and homonymy
'ring' has two different interpretations. 다른  part of speech 를  가지게  되어  structure difference 를

야기한다. Mary saw a nose ring which John owns - noun 으로  쓰임. Mary saw John's nose which

rings - verb 로  쓰임. (이부분에서  다른  분들  쓰신  것처럼  피어싱,  악세사리나  뭐  snoring  이런

단어를  쓰지  않았습니다..  감점이  됐을지는  잘  모르겠습니다!  지금  문제를  보니  각  단어의

meaning  쓰라는  말은  없어서  감점이  안되었거나  아주  작게  되었다고  예상하는  부분입니다)

Firstly. Orarely is usually case. (in)carefully is 'slowly case. Secondly, © - It is rare that John talks with
philosophers. It is rarely the case that John comes late for dass (i)- 'It is slow that the fish swims. 'It is

Firstly, there is a positive effect on the economy of disposable products and durable products. The
first example is related to disposable products. The products are made for short-term usage. The
employment of many workers and designs are required to manufacture them. The second example
is durable products. It requires the support of secondary industries to do repairs and supply parts ->
economic advantages in long-standing.
Secondly, there is a different effect on the environment btw disposable Inroducts and durable
products. The first example is disposable products. It causes many of waste and do not easily
decompose. Therefore it gives negative effects on environment The second example is durable
products. It could cut emissions of pollutants.
In addition, they include less landfill expansion and residual waste.
Firstly, students like the lesson which includes authentic, real materials such as cooking magazine, the
recipe. The first reason is that Sum says she is motivated to use the recipe and expressions that is
practical  and  authentic.  The  second  reason  is  that  Inho  feels  fun  and  can  clearly  understand  the
meaning in the real-life context
Secondly,  the  problem  is  that  the  students  dislike  the  teacher's  immediate  corrective  feedback
because  students  do  not  have  the  chance  for  self-repair.  The  first  solution  is  related  to  individual
aspect.  Students  should  have  spare  time  for  self-correction.  Students  can  find  out  the  errors.  The
second solution is related to the aspect of pair work. Students have a time to find the errors and correct
the errors. Students can notice the gap btw what they should say and what they want to say.

The adverb ‘rarely’ in (i) is a usually type, whereas the adverb ‘slowly’ in (ii) is a carefully type. / The
sentence (i) can be paraphrased as either the sentence ‘It is rare that John talks with philosophers.’
or ‘It is rarely the case that John talks with philosophers,’ as is the case with the sentence containing
usually. However, the sentence (ii) cannot be paraphrased as such, resulting in ungrammatical
sentences such as ‘*It is slow that the fish swims.’ and ‘*It is slowly the case that the fish swims.’
1st paragraph: Both disposable and durable products have a positive influence in terms of economy
in different ways. ①First of all, disposable products contribute to the growth of the economy,

because they need to be constantly manufactured to replace the products. ②Durable products
boost the growth of secondary industries that supply parts and repair them in order to make them
usable again. / 2nd paragraph: While disposable products do nothing but harm to the environment,
durable ones are good for the environment. ①Disposable products create a lot of waste, which is

hard to decompose. ②Durable products are used for a longer period of time, thus making less waste
and pollutants, which leads to less landfill expansion.

 Good point: The use of authentic materials ①more interesting ②provide contexts / Bad point: The

way the teacher corrects students’ errors ①Instead of explicitly correcting their errors, T can use

questions or incomplete sentences to provide Ss with the opportunities to self-correct. ②T can
encourage other Ss to correct Ss’ errors, using pair work or group work.

The sentence where the underlined part qualifies as a constituent, a noun phrase here, is (2). The
syntactic category is a noun phrase. According to the substitution test that only a constituent can be
replaced with pronouns like 'it' and 'them', the underlined part of (2) can be replaced with 'them as
illustrated in the grammatical sentence 'Call them in a week'. The underlined part (1) can't be replaced
with 'it' as shown in the ungrammatical sentence Can you confirm for membership?' The same is true
of (3) and (4).

sonorant] feature while the second has [-sonorant] feature.
